1935.04.29

Replacement Order for the Security Force; Already Issued by the Newly Established Provincial Government; Yin Rugeng Meets with Yu Xuezhong; Reports on Meeting with Yi Wo 1

(Beiping) The replacement order for the Security Force of the War Zone has been issued by the Hebei Provincial Government. Tao Shangming went to Yushu (present-day Kaiyuan) a few days ago to visit and discuss matters with Yi Wo, the head of the Japanese Special Service Agency stationed in Yushu. He has returned to Tangshan to preside over the rotation of the Security Force in that area. Yin Rugeng has finished his business in Tianjin and arrived in Beiping this morning. It is heard that Yin Rugeng will not stay in Beiping for long and will go to Tongxian tomorrow to preside over everything. The Security Force is expected to be mobilized no later than the beginning of next month. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

(Beiping) Yu Xuezhong came to Beiping a few days ago to visit He and to celebrate the birthday of Madame Song. After finishing these matters, he went to Tianjin this morning. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

(Tianjin) Yu Xuezhong returned to Tianjin from Beiping on the afternoon of the 28th. Yin Rugeng arrived at the Provincial Government in the afternoon to meet with him and report on the results of the negotiations with Yi Wo, which took place on the 26th in Yuguan (Shanhaiguan), regarding the war zone issues. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

(Tianjin) Shanhaiguan reports that Gu Tong, Tao Shangming, and Yin Rugeng arrived in Shanhaiguan at 10:00 AM on the 26th. Yi Wo, the head of the Japanese Special Service Agency, boarded the train to meet with them and talked until they reached Xingcheng outside the pass, where he parted ways with Gu Tong. Yi Wo, Tao Shangming, and Gu Rugeng toured the Xingcheng Hot Springs and discussed everything. He returned to Yushu on the morning of the 27th. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

(Tianjin) Yin Rugeng returned to Beiping by car from Tianjin at 1:30 PM on the 28th. It is heard that the handover of the old and new Security Forces is prepared and ready, and an order can be issued immediately to mobilize them. Li Yunsheng's unit in Yan Jiao will also be reduced in size within days. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 28th)

Yin Tong Goes to Shenyang to Japan; To Attend Tourism Conference 2

(Shenyang) Gu Tong, who arrived in Shenyang yesterday on the 26th, met with Kanto Army Special Service Agency Chief Doihara Kenji and Railway Bureau cadres on the 27th, and after various discussions, he attended a banquet hosted by the General Bureau that night. He departed from Shenyang for Japan at 11:00 PM in the afternoon. (Nichi-Ren dispatch from the 27th)

(Tokyo) The reason for the visit to Japan by Yin Tong, the head of the Bei Ning Railway Bureau, is to attend the East Asia Tourism Conference to be held in Tokyo on May 2nd. He is scheduled to arrive at Tokyo Station at 7:10 AM on the 30th of this month. (Nichi-Ren dispatch from the 28th)

Guizhou Bandits Fleeing to Pan County 3

Kunming Military News: (1) The main force of the bandits is fleeing towards Pan County. Wu's column, Liang's and Xiao's divisions, are following closely behind. The bandit's left flank, 3,000 strong, is fleeing directly towards Yangchang. An's brigade is following the rear of the bandits. (2) An's brigade telegraphed Long Yun, stating that they made contact with the rear of the bandits at Xiaoyangchang on the afternoon of the 24th for about two hours, killing hundreds, capturing five. The bandits fled towards Pan County. At 4:00 AM on the 25th, they made contact with the bandits again near Shazhai, fighting for several hours. The bandits fought and retreated, and after our pursuit and attack, we reached Baishi Rock at 3:00 PM in the afternoon, killing about 200 bandits along the way and capturing over 100 guns. Our side suffered over 30 casualties and is still pursuing fiercely. (3) Li Baobing arrived in Pingyi on the afternoon of the 25th. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 27th)

Guiyang The main force of the communist bandits is currently fleeing between Qujing and Zhan Yi, and the Second Route Army is rushing to pursue them. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 27th)

(Paris) According to news from Vietnam received by the Colonial Department, Chinese communist bandits are being pursued by government troops and have fled to the area near the Kuai Ze River on the border of Yunnan and Guizhou, attempting to escape into Sichuan, but have been surrounded by government troops. It seems that the communist bandit rebellion is still far from the Vietnamese border and does not pose any danger or threaten the Yunnan-Vietnam Railway. However, the Vietnamese authorities have taken precautionary measures on the border. (Havas dispatch from the 27th)

Wu Zhongxin and Others Arrive in Hankou 4

(Hankou) Wu Zhongxin, accompanied by Cao Jingyuan, concurrently head of the Guizhou Provincial Committee and Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, Ye Yuanlong, Director of the Department of Education, Zhang Dong, Secretary-General, and Mei Guangyu, Secretary, arrived in Hankou at noon on the 28th aboard the Ning Shao wheel steamer. They are staying at the Taipingzhi Hotel and will visit He Chengjun and Wang Weiying, etc., members of the Guizhou Provincial Committee staying in Hankou. They are scheduled to take a plane to Chongqing and then to Guizhou on the 29th to establish the provincial government first, and then schedule the inauguration ceremony and take the oath of office. According to Wu's entourage, Wu has already consulted with Kong once regarding the reorganization of finances. Other policy guidelines will be determined after consulting with Chiang Kai-shek. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

Chiang Kai-shek Rewards; Li Yunjie's Division 5

Guiyang Li Yunjie, commander of the 27th Army and concurrently commander of the 23rd Division, arrived in Guiyang yesterday afternoon with his troops. Chiang Kai-shek, considering that the commander had traveled a long distance in pursuing and suppressing the remaining bandits, specially rewarded each unit of the division with wine, meat, and 1,440 silver dollars. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 27th)

Sichuan Provincial Government to Move to Chengdu 6

(Chongqing) Deng Mingjie, the secretary-general of the provincial government, told reporters that the renovation of the provincial government's buildings in Chengdu is nearing completion and will be moved there soon. Chairman Liu was previously ill due to overwork, but has now recovered and is recuperating. He will be able to resume his duties in a few days and plans to personally lead provincial government officials to Chengdu to direct the military suppression of the bandits. Xu's bandits are fleeing westward, and the encirclement is already formed. The extermination date is not far off. There are heavy troops stationed in Chengdu, and public sentiment has become stable. Sichuan has established 18 administrative inspectorate districts, and candidates for the special commissioners of 13 districts have already been internally decided and are being telegraphed to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek for instructions. After approval, they will be established separately. In addition, the provincial government will improve the district organizations under the counties. After the first phase of the county administration training institute is completed, they will be assigned as county magistrates, secretaries, section chiefs, and district chiefs. The provincial government is also compiling the policy plan for the 24th year. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 28th)

Seven District Supervisors; Inaugurated Today 7

(Nanjing) At the National Government's memorial week on the morning of the 29th, Yu Youren will attend and report. After the memorial week, the seven district supervisors, including Fang Juehui, will hold an inauguration ceremony in the government, and Chairman Lin will deliver instructions. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 28th)

(Nanjing) Yu Youren and Ding Chaowu arrived in Nanjing from Shanghai by train on the 28th. Fang Juehui and Dai Kuisheng also returned from Shanghai in the afternoon. At 7:00 PM, Yu hosted a dinner at his residence, inviting Ding Weifen and the seven supervisors, including Wang Luyi. During the dinner, they discussed the location of the supervisors' offices, as well as issues such as funding, organization, and powers. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 28th)

Russian Ambassador Arrives in Nanjing Yesterday; Scheduled to Visit Premier Wang This Morning 8

(Nanjing) Soviet Ambassador Bogomolov and his wife, as well as Counselor Oshanin, arrived in Nanjing from Shanghai on the 28th. They are scheduled to visit Premier Wang at the Ministry of Railways official residence on the morning of the 29th for a courtesy call after returning to their post. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

(Nanjing) Soviet Ambassador Bogomolov, accompanied by Chinese Secretary Oshanin, arrived in Nanjing by train from Shanghai on the morning of the 28th. The secretary of the Soviet Embassy in Nanjing, Meyne, led embassy staff to the station to greet them. After the Ambassador got off the train, he went to the embassy to rest. He is scheduled to visit Premier Wang at the Ministry of Railways official residence at 10:00 AM on the 29th for his first courtesy call after returning to his post. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 28th)

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Orders River Steamer; Specifically for Yangtze River Shipping 9

(Nanjing) The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company borrowed £400,000 from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity last year, originally planning to order four ocean-going vessels and four river steamers. However, due to insufficient funds, only four ocean-going vessels were purchased in the UK and shipped to China for use one after another. Now, with a remaining balance of tens of thousands of pounds from the Boxer Indemnity, it is planned to use this remaining balance to order a river steamer in China specifically for Yangtze River shipping. The Ministry has already submitted the plan to the Boxer Indemnity Commission for review. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

Manufacturers Participating in the National Exhibition; Arriving in Nanjing One After Another 10

(Nanjing) According to the Ministry of Industry, manufacturers from Shanghai and Hangzhou participating in the National Products Exhibition have arrived in Nanjing one after another. Manufacturers led by the Shanghai National Products Factories Association arrived in Nanjing at 6:00 PM on the 28th. Approximately 300 people, including the association's organizers and manufacturers, are present. The goods from each factory are scheduled to be unloaded and transported to the venue on the 29th. The booth locations will be drawn at a meeting on the morning of the 29th, and setup will begin in the afternoon. A total of more than 130 factories are participating in this exhibition. A variety show is planned for several days during the exhibition, which will open on the 1st. Liu Weichi will preside over the event. The planning is currently underway. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

He Yingqin Left Beiping for Jinan Yesterday; To Inspect Troops and Visit Qingdao 11

(Beiping) He Yingqin left Beiping for Jinan this afternoon to tour scenic spots in Shandong Province. This morning, he convened a meeting at the Military Affairs Commission, inviting the heads of various departments, section chiefs, and officers above the rank of colonel to give instructions. This afternoon, he hosted a banquet for Gao Lingbai, Yu Feipeng, and others, which ended around 2:00 PM. At 4:30 PM, He, accompanied by his secretary Xie Boyuan, staff officer Hou Cheng, and others, took a car to the station outside Guang'anmen. A special train was prepared on the Beiping-Nanjing Railway. Wan Fulin, Shang Zhen, Bao Wenwei, Song Zheyuan, and others went to the station to see him off. It is heard that He will transfer to the Beiping-Nanjing Railway at Fengtai and go directly to Jinan. He may visit scenic spots along the way. After staying in Jinan briefly, he will go to Qingdao and other places to inspect. Beiping has already telegraphed Shandong and Korea to report his departure. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

(Tianjin) He Yingqin arrived in Tianjin at 7:30 PM on the 28th. The special train consisted of eight cars, including second and third class cars, headed by engine group leader Xie Zhongwen and 40 others, as well as a platoon of guards. The train stopped at the main station. Yu Xuezhong, accompanied by the heads of various departments and bureaus and Mayor Zhang, boarded the train to meet and talk with him. He left Nankai for Jinan at 8:20 PM. Xie Zhongyuan said that He would inspect Qingdao and Jinan for one day and would return to Beiping after a day's stay. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

(Beiping) He Yingqin, the chairman of the Beiping Military Affairs Commission, took a special train to Jinan on the 28th for inspection. A special train was prepared by the Beiping-Nanjing Railway Bureau and arrived at the Guang'anmen Station of the Beiping-Suiyuan Railway at 1:00 PM in the afternoon for standby use. The entourage and guards boarded the train successively at 3:00 PM. At 10:00 AM, He convened a meeting of senior officials at the Military Affairs Commission to give instructions. He returned to the Jurentang (benevolence hall) headquarters for a rest at noon. At 4:40 PM, he arrived at the station, exchanged pleasantries with the welcoming personnel, and boarded the special train, ordering it to depart. It departed at 4:45 PM, heading south through Fengtai. Song Zheyuan, Fu Zuoyi, Shang Zhen, Xu Tingyao, Guan Linzheng, Yu Feipeng, Qin Dechun, Xiao Zhenying, Bao Wenwei, Yin Rugeng, Yu Jinshu, and the members, heads, and section chiefs of the Military Affairs Commission, totaling over 100 people, went to the station to see him off. Wei Zonghan, a member of the Military Affairs Commission, Xiao Renyuan, a senior staff officer, and Xie Zhenyuan, the chief secretary, also accompanied him. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 28th)

(Beiping) He Yingqin, the chairman of the Beiping Military Affairs Commission, has been in Beiping for more than two years. Apart from one visit to Ningxia and Suiyuan last year, he has never visited anywhere else. Recently, taking advantage of his free time, he took a special train with a few staff members and guards to Jinan at 4:45 PM on the afternoon of the 28th to inspect the troops in the area. He is expected to arrive on the morning of the 29th. If time permits, he may visit Qingdao and return in about a week. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 28th)

(Qingdao) Ge Guangting, the chairman of the Jiaozhou Railway Commission, took the night train to Jinan at 9:40 PM on the 28th to welcome General He. According to talks, He is expected to arrive in Jinan on the 30th and may come to Qingdao that night. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

Big Sword Society Bandits Discovered in Xinglong Mountain North of the Great Wall 12

(Tianjin) On the 25th, more than 100 Big Sword Society bandits were discovered in Xinglong Mountain north of the Great Wall. The bandits were led by a certain Li from Yutian and invaded Xinglong, engaging in battle with the puppet Japanese army. They exchanged fire for several hours, resulting in the death of one sergeant and two soldiers, and the injury of two soldiers on the Japanese side. On the puppet army side, one died and four were injured. The bandits abandoned over ten bodies and fled outside the Great Wall. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

Completion of Barracks for the Japanese Military Police in Yuguan 13

(Beiping) The Japanese military police in Yuguan, which previously built barracks with 100,000 yuan, have been completed. Representatives from Japanese and puppet organizations in Yuguan participated. The commander of the Japanese military police, Anshansuke, and squad leader Cangzuo, and others, were responsible for the reception. The Japanese military police in Yuguan have all moved to the new site. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

China Prepares to Participate in the International Lawyers Conference 14

(Nanjing) The International Lawyers Conference will be held in Brussels in early July this year. It is necessary for the Chinese Lawyers Association to participate. Liu Lumin requested instructions from Minister of Justice Wang Yongbin, and discussed matters such as funding and the selection of representatives. It was discussed once at the Suzhou Standing Committee of the Lawyers Association on January 5th, and a decision can be made soon. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

Organization of the National Medical Hall; Not Subject to Party Guidance 15

(Nanjing) The Central People's Movement Committee requested an explanation regarding whether the organizational system of the National Medical Hall should be subject to the guidance of the Party. The Executive Yuan replied, stating that "the hall is an academic organization and not a mass organization. The Party does not need to provide guidance, and its branches and sub-branches should not interfere with health administration." (Special dispatch from the 28th)

Ministry of Finance Limits Issuance of Banknotes by Local Banks 16

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance requested the central government to limit the issuance of banknotes by local banks. The method is that, regardless of whether it is a newly established local bank or one that has already been established, in addition to the amount previously approved by the Ministry, if there is a request to issue more banknotes for the purpose of regulating circulation, they will be allowed to use banknotes from the Central Bank and issue auxiliary coins for circulation in order to show the restriction. This method can only be approved after the request has been examined and verified to be true. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

Articles of Association of China and Communications Banks; Submitted to the Ministry of Finance for Revision 17

(Nanjing) After China and Communications Banks increased capital by adding official shares, the articles of association of the two banks were submitted to the Ministry of Finance. The competent department revised them and submitted them to the Executive Yuan for review and amendment. In addition to increasing the amount of capital and adding official share directors, the interest rate was revised to 5% for official shares and 7% for commercial shares. (Note that the 7% for commercial shares is the same as before the increase in official shares.) There were no changes to the scope of business management. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

Nanjing Municipal Government Requests; Restriction on the Requisition of Private Land 18

Huge Requisitions Greatly Hinder People's Livelihood; When Needed, Purchase Should Be the Principle

(Nanjing) The Nanjing Municipal Government reported that in recent times, various agencies in Nanjing have been requisitioning land for construction, often exceeding the amount actually needed. The land requisitioned often amounts to hundreds or thousands of acres, and the number of households affected can reach dozens or even hundreds. After the landowners are requisitioned, their source of production is cut off, and they are forced to scatter and flee. Although land requisition has compensation for land prices, excessive requisition and insufficient compensation, the income from the official land price is only 10% to 50% of the actual value. Even if the compensation is adequate, those who are accustomed to their old businesses, getting the money but losing the land, also find it difficult to make a living. Such large-scale requisition cases greatly hinder people's livelihood. The Municipal Government has submitted the report to the Executive Yuan, requesting the National Government to instruct various agencies in Nanjing to restrict requisitioning of land in the future, except for opening roads, constructing schools, and other public facilities that benefit the local people. In the future, the principle of purchasing should be followed when private land is needed. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

Daokou-Qinghua Railway Extending Route; Funding is Being Negotiated 19

(Nanjing) The Daokou-Qinghua Railway extends from Daokou to Daming, with a construction cost of 3 million yuan, of which 2.2 million yuan is for materials, which can be paid in installments. 500,000 yuan will be raised by the railway bureau itself, and the remaining 1.3 million yuan will need to be borrowed from outside. Director Fan Yu came to Nanjing, met with Vice Minister of Railways Zeng Zhongming, and went to Shanghai to negotiate with the banking community and the Fu Company respectively, hoping that the Fu Company could undertake a larger amount of the 1.3 million yuan, and the banking community could undertake a smaller amount. The banking side indicated that they could help with tens of thousands of yuan. Since the Fu Company's representative in Shanghai could not make a decision, they telegraphed the London headquarters for instructions. Fan first returned to Nanjing. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

Yu Jingtang; Goes to Xuzhou to Inspect Politics 20

(Xuzhou) Su Provincial Commissioner of Civil Affairs Yu Jingtang, together with Ye Xiufeng, a standing member of the Anti-Smoking Association, and 20 others, arrived in Xuzhou from Zhenjiang this morning on the Shanghai-Beiping train to inspect political performance and the suppression of smoking. Special Commissioner Shao Hanyuan and representatives from all walks of life welcomed them at the station. Yu and Ye went to various administrative agencies and drug rehabilitation centers to inspect and tour scenic spots this afternoon. They attended a banquet hosted by Shao in the evening. It was decided that the police of the four counties of Tongshan, Suining, Fengxian, and Pei will be inspected on the 29th. The police teams have now gathered in Xuzhou and are preparing to be reviewed. According to Yu's statement to reporters, this trip is specifically to investigate the administration of Xuzhou. He attaches great importance to the construction of the Xuzhou area and plans to have a concrete plan after the inspection. In general, the construction of the Xuzhou area should prioritize water conservancy. The province will provide assistance to the extent that the local forces can afford, which will be enough to develop the construction. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

(Xuzhou) Su Provincial Commissioner of Civil Affairs Yu Jingtang, Provincial Anti-Smoking Association Standing Committee Member Ye Xiufeng, accompanied by police inspectors Zhu Aizhou, Zhang Henyu, and Ye Fengsheng, Dai Shiying, etc., arrived in Xuzhou from Zhenjiang on the morning of the 28th. Leaders of various agencies and county magistrates of Xuzhou welcomed them at the station. Yu and others stayed at the Huayuan Hotel and inspected various agencies in the afternoon. It was decided that the public security police of the four counties of Tongshan, Xiao, Pei, and Dang will be inspected on the 29th. According to Yu, he came to inspect the administrative construction, Baojia security, general rural conditions of Xubei Xuzhou counties, and review the military forces of the counties, stay in Xuzhou for two days, and then visit the counties of Xiao Dang Feng Pei. The provincial government attaches the same importance to the construction of various counties. Although the Jiangnan highway is more developed, water conservancy in Jiangbei is already underway. At present, they are handling the compilation and investigation of Baojia land reports, and vigorously implementing the work of banning smoking. Ye said that this came specifically to inspect the smoking cessation results of the counties. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 28th)

Gale Winds Resurge in Tianjin 21

(Tianjin) Gale winds resurged in Tianjin at 11:00 PM on the 28th. Sand and dust were raised several feet, making it impossible for people to open their eyes. The temperature dropped, and many telephones were out of service. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

(Beiping) The telephone lines in Beiping and Tianjin, which were previously damaged by strong winds, have been repaired this morning. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

(Tianjin) The Hebei Provincial Government has received reports that the counties affected by wind and drought include Changping, Jinghai, Rongcheng, Dongguang, Tongxian, Lutai, and Yutian. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

(Tianjin) On the 27th, the wind in Tangshan did not stop. More than 100 trees were uprooted in Dongluan Village. The house of Wang Qingchen, a resident, was blown down, and the roof was spinning in the sky. Fifty earthen houses in the Haoshen Temple in the eastern pottery kiln of Tangshan City were blown down. Dust and sand covered the sky, and the vegetables in the gardens were all uprooted by the wind. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

Strong Winds on the Luan River; Cargo Ships Capsized Mid-Voyage 22

(Tianjin) Due to strong winds on the Luan River, the shipping bureau has prohibited ships from sailing for two consecutive encounters. Ships gathered at various docks like ants. On the 26th, the wind subsided slightly, and eight cargo ships carrying vegetables sailed out in violation of the order. They encountered wind mid-voyage and all capsized. Nine boatmen were rescued, three drowned, and six went missing. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

Earthquake Occurs in Fengrun 23

(Tianjin) An earthquake occurred in Fengrun County at 7:30 PM on the 26th for 30 seconds. At the beginning, there was a sound of rumbling that went from southeast to west. Within 30 miles of the city, doors and windows shook with noise. Fortunately, the time was very short. Except for the collapse of one pit in the old Guandi Temple in Hanzhuang, there was no other damage. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

Circulating Clinic Method in the Changyuan Disaster Area 24

(Tianjin) The Hebei-Henan Disaster Relief Committee formulated a method for circulating clinics in the Changyuan disaster area, establishing a team consisting of one team leader, one doctor, and two nurses, which will depart from the province to work. Ye Zhenmin, a member of the Hebei Civil Affairs Department, telegraphed the province, stating that the Changyuan City Defense Committee has ended, the water flow has been cut off, and transportation has gradually recovered. The silted fields have cracked and need to be sown urgently. The Changyuan city wall has been eroded by water for a long time, and many parts have collapsed. It should be repaired quickly to prevent unforeseen circumstances. The Taihang dyke must be repaired to be high, thick, and strong to prepare for emergencies. Zhang County is currently planning and will submit it to the province in a few days. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

Qinhuangdao's Market is Depressed 25

(Tianjin) Qinhuangdao's economy is depressed due to rampant gambling, with as many as three Huahui clubs. Men and women are addicted and do not work. Seven more stores went bankrupt this month. (Special dispatch from the 28th)

Commentary

The Premise of Chinese Industrial Control 33

— Ren

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce believes that the reasons for the increasing decline of industry in our country are: (1) The industrial sector is like a heap of loose sand, insufficient to resist the dumping of foreign industrial products. (2) The industries in our country squeeze each other, resulting in overproduction. Therefore, it specially submitted a request to the Executive Yuan to implement industrial controls in order to save our country's industry, which is on the verge of collapse. Before the Great War, the economic thinking of the world mostly advocated laissez-faire economics, emphasizing free competition, and following the laws of natural selection. After the Great War, the thinking changed drastically. Most countries advocated controlled economics, seeking planning and control in all production and consumption. When the world panic occurred and the Soviet Union's Five-Year Plan was completed, the trend of controlled thinking became more prevalent. Gradually, today, it has further advanced to the "Autarky" of national economicism. However, laissez-faire economics and controlled economics are inherently products of the evolution of the times. Before and after the 18th-century Industrial Revolution, new technologies were not yet developed, and the old systems were shaking. It was inevitable to hope that a laissez-faire economic policy would promote the gradual development of a new economic society. However, today, more than a hundred years after the Industrial Revolution, the economic society produced by the Industrial Revolution has many drawbacks. Therefore, one cannot but hope for a controlled economic policy to correct them. For this reason, the transition of various countries from laissez-faire economics to controlled economics all has a relationship with their historical environment. The policy itself has no absolute good or evil.

However, the situation in our country today is not entirely similar to that of other countries. Therefore, if our country also implements economic controls today, its goals, steps, and methods must also be different from those of other countries. To elaborate, other countries implement controls because of the development of production and the desire to maintain the existing economic system. Therefore, when they implement controls, they only seek to prevent overproduction, which is sufficient. However, our country today implements controls because of the backwardness of production, and to transform the economy. It is clearly insufficient to only seek a reduction in production and the non-aggression of the same industry.

In recent years, there has also been talk of overproduction in China. However, this is only a superficial phenomenon. In reality, if the current production is evenly distributed among 500 million people, it is not only not excessive, but also insufficient. Therefore, the so-called surplus is actually an unnatural surplus. This unnatural surplus is due to the narrow sales channels of products. Therefore, the current problems facing China's industry lie in how to seek sales channels for industrial products, improve the economic status quo, and increase the purchasing power of the people. That is the first thing. Seeking improvement in production technology to reduce production costs is the second thing. Resisting foreign goods to preserve economic strength is the third thing. If we can strive to complete these three things, and add thorough controls, then how can China's current situation not be improved? Otherwise, if all the conditions for developing industry are not met, and we rashly implement controls to reduce production or maintain the status quo, then I am afraid that the effect of the controls will not be seen, but it will give foreign goods the opportunity to dump at low prices. This is something that the Chinese people must not fail to observe.

British Military Officers Secretly Discuss Reorganizing Far East Garrison, Close Cooperation Between Navy, Army, and Air Force, U.S. Fleet Conducts Large-Scale Maneuvers in the Pacific 34

(London) A "Daily Express" report states that naval, army, and air force generals held a secret meeting at the Campbell Military Academy to discuss the thorough reorganization of the British naval and air forces in the Far East and to formulate a cooperation plan between the navy, army, and air force. The level of close cooperation is unprecedented in British history. The generals, in view of the mutual constraints and delays in military agencies during the European War, have also agreed on methods of improvement. (Havas dispatch, 28th)

Saint Peter, USA. The plan for the U.S. fleet's large-scale Pacific maneuvers has now been completed and is ready to depart at any time upon order. The most famous of the maneuver plans is "Problem Sixteen." The details are still kept secret by the naval authorities. However, it is understood that this maneuver will pay special attention to the defense of the islands along the Alaskan coast and the sea area between Midway Island and Pearl Harbor. Early next week, 153 warships will depart from here and Pearl Harbor. The maneuvers will officially begin on May 3. The "attacking" fleet will be led by Commander Hepburn, while the "defending" fleet along the Pacific coast will be commanded by Commander Laning. In terms of air power, in addition to the aircraft carried on the maneuvering warships, there will be 430 other aircraft participating at the same time. (National Telegram, 27th)

U.S. Naval Exercises, Japan Has No Need to Be Suspicious, More Than Two Thousand Miles Away from Japanese Territory, U.S. Supports Resumption of Naval Talks 35

(Washington) The naval and government authorities are very puzzled by the claim in Japanese newspapers that the United States is unwilling to resume naval talks and are strongly denying any action that has given rise to this impression. The United States has repeatedly expressed its support for continuing the London Conference. However, the United States particularly wants Britain to initiate it. Since Japan demanded naval equality, leading to the breakdown of the conference, there has been no exchange of official documents between countries regarding this matter to date. At the same time, Commander Stanley, Director of the Naval Personnel Assignment Office, told the Associated Press that the naval exercises to be held next week are not an action against Japan. During all the exercises, the U.S. fleet will be more than two thousand miles away from Japan proper. (National Telegram, 27th)

Foreign Islands Near the U.S., Enemies Can Use as an Advantage, Should Be Seized First in Case of Emergency, Recommendation by General Andrews 36

(Washington) U.S. Air Force leader General Andrews told the House Military Affairs Committee today that the United States must be prepared to seize British and French islands near the U.S. coast in an emergency. There are many bases outside the coast that can be used by the enemy, such as Newfoundland, Bermuda, Jamaica, and Trinidad. If the situation is indeed urgent, these coastal bases must be seized to prevent the enemy from using them to attack us. General Andrews did not specify what he meant by an emergency situation. It was subsequently heard that at the continued hearing of the Military Affairs Committee, Air Force Headquarters Major Cole stated that he had heard from reliable sources that an unnamed powerful Asian country is currently using hundreds of instructors to train the Peruvian army. He also said that one day, we may suddenly learn that the Panama Canal has been attacked and seized as the first step before a declaration of war. This is not impossible. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

The Senate will also pass it without amendment. The U.S. Navy has increased the construction of 44 ships that have already started construction in the 1934 and 1935 fiscal years. The new ships added in these two years total 68 ships, and a large expansion plan has been implemented. Total above: Forty-four ships

Submarines: Six ships

Total above: Twenty-four ships

Scheduled to start construction in the 1935 fiscal year

In total, 12 warships will be built this year.

Italy

Battleships: Two ships

Based on the figures listed above, it is clear that the major naval powers are seeking to expand their naval strength. (Japan News Agency, 28th)

(London) Yesterday's "Daily Telegraph" reported on German air force armaments, saying that the number of first-line aircraft in that country has more than doubled that of Britain. Germany Violates Treaty to Reorganize Navy, Britain Considers Countermeasures, Cabinet Calls Special Meeting This Morning, Naval Talks Between the Two Countries May Be Postponed 39

(London) According to the "Observer's" diplomatic correspondent, the British cabinet will hold a special meeting on Monday morning to discuss Germany's reorganization of its navy (Germany has decided to build 12 submarines) and to consider the actions Britain should take, such as lodging a protest with Germany, or postponing the naval talks between Britain and Germany next month. (Havas dispatch, 27th)

(Berlin) Officials refuse to comment on rumors that Germany is violating the treaty by building several submarines. However, according to diplomatic sources, senior German naval personnel have recently been very active in seeking information on the latest post-war submarines and bombers. According to unverified rumors, the German government has ordered several submarines from the Stone State Shipyard, and the engines needed will be built at the Irping Factory. (Reuters dispatch, 28th)

(London) Naval experts from Britain and Germany were originally scheduled to hold informal talks in early May. According to the "Daily Herald," a mouthpiece of the Labour Party, Germany will propose a request at the talks to be allowed to build five high-sided armored cruisers, seven dreadnoughts, sixteen cruisers, fifty torpedo boat destroyers, and fifty submarines. It is expected that Britain will definitely reject this, and Germany will implement this plan regardless of whether Britain allows it or not. The newspaper also said that Germany has recently decided to build 12 submarines immediately. This is not what Britain wants to hear, and the naval experts' talks between Britain and Germany are very likely to be cancelled. (Havas dispatch, 26th)

Concluding Mutual Assistance Pact, France and Russia Resume Negotiations, Fundamental Principles Agreed Upon, Now Awaiting Instructions from Moscow 40

(Paris) Soviet Ambassador Potemkin continued to discuss the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact with Foreign Minister Laval, which lasted for more than two hours. The two sides exchanged views and reviewed the articles submitted by the other. Potemkin intends to report the results of the talks in the past two days to his government before continuing the discussions. The general impression is still smooth. The Soviet government is making efforts to understand the views of France (France advocates that the Mutual Assistance Pact should be integrated with the constraints stipulated in the Locarno Pact). The work of organizing the articles of the Mutual Assistance Pact can be completed in the middle of next week, and Laval and Potemkin will initial it. When Laval goes to Russia at the beginning of next month, he will formally sign it. In addition to the important personnel of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the legal advisor of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Bartbain, also participated in today's talks. (Havas dispatch, 27th)

(Paris) The negotiations between France and Russia on the Mutual Assistance Pact have not yet been finalized. Soviet Ambassador Potemkin and French Foreign Minister Laval met for more than two hours yesterday afternoon. According to semi-official sources, the two diplomats thoroughly discussed several unresolved points. Potemkin has now reported to Moscow and, after receiving a reply, will resume negotiations with the French Foreign Minister tomorrow or Tuesday. It is heard that the two governments have completely agreed on the fundamental principle of mutual assistance within the framework of the League of Nations Covenant. However, the Russian government is willing to take military action first, followed by the procedures of the League of Nations. The French government's wishes are exactly the opposite. It is expected that a compromise can be reached in the end. Although it does not stipulate automatic military action, it will make actions in accordance with the League of Nations Covenant more convenient and practical. It is now believed that the pact will be initialed next week when the French Foreign Minister goes to Moscow. (Reuters dispatch, 28th)

(Paris) It is said today that the military alliance between France and Russia has been delayed again. Spokespersons for both governments have stated that this delay is a technical issue. Both countries are satisfied with the terms of the draft. However, because the current draft has several insignificant modifications from the original, it will not be effective until it has been approved by Moscow. It is said that the pact can be signed on Tuesday, at which time the Soviet Russian representative will meet with French Foreign Minister Laval again. (National Telegram, 28th)

Lyon. Edouard Herriot, leader of the Radical Socialist Party and minister without portfolio, recently spoke at a meeting of the party's executive committee on Franco-German relations and the attitude that the party should take in the nationwide municipal council elections on May 5. Herriot called on Republicans to unite and fight against those on the left and right who advocate tyrannical theories, and especially to denounce those who promote revolution and oppose the completion of national defense. He said that loving peace as always should be sought in security, and that all nations have the right to enjoy security. Herriot then referred to the Declaration issued by Britain, France, Germany, Italy, and the United States on December 11, 1932, granting Germany equal rights to armaments, saying, "Although our connection with Germany has been interrupted, we still believe that it is possible to continue it. We must work hard and dedicate our lives to it, but we will not allow ourselves to be insulted or humiliated." (Havas dispatch, 27th)

(Paris) Edouard Herriot, who has been vigorously advocating the conclusion of the Franco-Russian Entente, was suddenly cursed by French communists today while giving a speech in Lyon on the rationality of France's implementation of a two-year military service system. Herriot repeatedly stated how warmly he was welcomed by Soviet Russia when he was in Moscow, but he still could not dispel the anger of the French communists. As a result, Herriot was forced to step down and the meeting adjourned. (National Telegram, 27th)

In addition, the government has launched new taxes, and the actual revenue is far above expectations, which can also be used for this purpose, so raising funds is very easy. Tatarescu announced that the government has signed a contract with the Czech Skoda armaments factory to undertake various army equipment. In 1932, Romanian police found some suspicious documents in the Skoda factory's office in Bucharest and arrested the factory representative, Serezheski, and sentenced him to prison for espionage. This case has been pending for a long time. Today, Finance Minister Endronescu announced to the National Defense Committee that the government has signed an agreement with the Skoda factory to completely resolve this county case, so the contract for undertaking army equipment can be signed smoothly. Germany to Promulgate Citizenship Law, Non-German Races, Deprived of Citizenship Rights 45

Jews Forbidden to Fly the German Flag and the Swastika Flag

(Berlin) It is heard that Germany will announce a citizenship law this year. Jews and non-Aryans will not be recognized as German citizens. According to Minister of the Interior Dr. Frick today, only people of Germanic race will be able to enjoy the qualifications of German citizens. The doctor also quoted Hitler's book, which describes the distinction between German people and German citizens. It says that only those whose parents are both Germanic can be German and can be German citizens. Their bodies must be strong, and their character must be pure. They must be granted citizenship after completing military service. The doctor also said that only those who serve the people and the country and prove their ability can obtain the honor of citizenship. Only citizens can hold public office, join the army, and have the right to vote. Those who receive citizenship must swear allegiance to the nation and the leader. People who are base and enemies of the state will be deprived of their citizenship fees. (Reuters dispatch, 28th)

(Berlin) German Interior Minister Frick today ordered Jews to be banned from flying the German flag and the swastika flag, as there have been repeated disturbances to public order due to Jews flying the above flags. (Reuters dispatch, 27th)

Germany Continues to Arrest Opposition Pastors, Cattle Like Sheep Enclosed in Concentration Camps 46

(Berlin) After the Evangelical Church pastors held their annual meeting in Hordeburg, they petitioned Hitler to allow the Langen Church to publicly preach against new heresies and to promptly abolish the current crackdown plan. However, given that several pastors and church officials have been arrested again this week, this petition seems to have had no effect. On Saturday and Sunday, two Evangelical Church pastors were arrested and released after questioning. However, one pastor who was also arrested on Saturday afternoon is still being held at the Secret Police Headquarters. At dusk on Saturday and Sunday, police searched the office of Niemöller, the leader of the opposition pastors, copied several documents, and detained two officials on suspicion of providing information to foreign newspapers. Currently, there are 35 opposition pastors detained in concentration camps. The hair of all the people has been shaved, and they have been subjected to various abuses. It is heard that many people in the Catholic districts have also been arrested, including several nuns. They have been imprisoned in the women's prison here for allegedly violating foreign exchange crackdown laws. However, Catholics believe that the nuns' arrests were caused by people framing them. (Reuters dispatch, 28th)

Netherlands in Financial Difficulty, Major Cuts in Government Expenses 47

The Hague. The government has now presented a bill to reduce public expenditure, including a broad plan of thrift. It is said that the economic situation in the Netherlands has been gradually difficult due to the development of the unfortunate international situation. It is estimated that the 1935 budget will be short of 73,000,000 guilders (936 will be short of 75,000,000 guilders. The total amount of savings is 97,000,000 guilders, of which 77,000,000 guilders are saved according to the new plan. The reduction in official salaries can save 10,000,000 guilders. May Day Celebrations Being Prepared in Austria, French Government Bans Parades and Demonstrations 49

Vienna. A grand celebration will be held here on May Day, Labor Day. Soviet Russia Develops Animal Husbandry 50

(Moscow) The People's Committee has recently decided to develop the country's animal husbandry, planning to increase 10 million cattle, 17 million pigs, 16 million sheep, and 2 million horses. After the Russian Civil War, animal husbandry declined greatly. The current government is working hard to revitalize it. In addition, the Food Commission has also decided to build a railway from Arta on the east coast of the Black Sea to Dugong to Akhalsiche. The road line requires the construction of 120 kilometers of embankments to avoid passing through Baku and bypassing the Caucasus Mountains, which can shorten the route by 700 kilometers. It is estimated that it will be completed by 1937. This road is extremely important in terms of economy, military strategy, and travel. After the road is built, the manganese produced by the Republic of Georgia can be transported to central and southern Russia via this road. (Havas dispatch, 28th)

Severe Earthquake Occurs on Portuguese Island in the Atlantic 51

Ponta Delgada, Azores Islands. A strong earthquake occurred this morning in the Azores Islands, a Portuguese territory in the Atlantic. The largest island in the archipelago, São Miguel Island, was most affected. The city of Vila Franca do Campo suffered the most deaths, injuries, and losses. When the first shock occurred here, residents were greatly frightened and ran outdoors. Fortunately, only a few houses collapsed, and only a few residents were injured. The Azores Islands are a volcanic area and often experience earthquakes. On August 31, 1926, the city of Horta on the island suffered a major earthquake, and the losses were extremely heavy. It is found that Ponta Delgada is the largest port among the islands. (Reuters dispatch, 28th)

Grand Occasion of International Film Conference 52

(Berlin) The International Film Conference held in Germany is a rare grand event, and a film dance party was held in the zoo. Many German stage stars participated, and Propaganda Minister Goebbels also attended. (National Telegram, 28th)

U.S. Treasury Department Considers Policy Change Overnight; How to Compensate China and Mexico for Losses; Silver Purchase Price Temporarily Unchanged; Mexico Implements New Currency System 53

(Washington) The Treasury Department was brightly lit tonight, with leaders of the New Deal debating two issues: whether to revise the silver policy and how to compensate China and Mexico for the losses they have suffered due to the U.S. silver program. (National Telegram, 27th)

(Washington) Treasury Secretary Morgenthau stated today that the government would not announce any changes to the price of purchasing domestically mined silver by the end of this week. Today, Democratic Senator McCarran told a new reporter that he had

(Washington) discussed the general silver situation with Treasury Secretary Morgenthau, but the Secretary did not indicate what actions the government would take. (Reuters, 27th) Treasury Secretary Morgenthau also announced today that the Treasury Department would not change the silver purchase price before next Monday. Prior to this announcement, reporters had been waiting for a long time, hoping that the government would issue an important statement at any moment, changing the silver policy. Observers believe that the Secretary's words today mean that the Treasury Department is working closely with President Roosevelt and is still considering several feasible methods. Before a definite policy is decided, the existing state will be maintained. On Wall Street, there are rumors that the government intends to drastically increase both gold and silver prices to prevent speculators from taking advantage of the government's monetary system plan. However, these rumors have not been confirmed by reliable sources. Democratic Senator McCarran consulted with the Treasury Secretary for a long time and later told the press that the Secretary has become more in favor of the plan to re-establish silver as the U.S. monetary standard at a price of $1.29 per ounce. Former Treasury officials and New Deal authorities are all paying close attention to the silver issue. The most concerned are the adverse results of the U.S. silver policy on China and Mexico. Now, the Bank of Mexico has completely closed, and the new currency system policy has taken effect. Mexican Finance Ministry Special Envoy Robles has arrived here by plane, preparing to consult with Treasury Secretary Morgenthau. However, Treasury officials said that Robles would not be able to meet with Morgenthau until the beginning of next week. It is reported that Robles will raise a serious protest against the U.S. silver policy in person. However, observers say that the U.S.'s new policy will also be decided before the protest is officially filed. The plans currently being considered by the Treasury Department are roughly as follows:

(1) Immediately set the Treasury Department's silver purchase price at $1.29; (2) Continue to purchase domestically produced raw silver at a price slightly higher than the world silver price; (3) Purchase entirely according to world market prices, without favoring domestically produced silver; (4) Purchase raw silver at a price of $1 per ounce.

The Treasury Secretary has repeatedly stated that the U.S. will continue to purchase silver until the silver price reaches $1.29, or until the Treasury's silver reserves reach a ratio of four parts silver to one part gold. Government leaders are paying close attention to the speculation that has arisen around the world. New Wall Street is rumored to believe that the government will immediately raise the silver price to the statutory maximum limit in order to prevent it. According to experts, the U.S. will probably not raise the silver price above $1.29, as this action would be tantamount to further devaluing the U.S. dollar. (National Telegram, 27th)

Mexico Bans Silver Exports

Mexico City: The Mexican government today implemented its newly enacted currency system policy, banning the export of silver coins and silver bars, and replacing various silver coins with paper money. All banks have been ordered to close until next Monday. Raw silver is not included under the export ban. The purpose of this ban is to prevent the melting of silver coins. Now, the government has nationalized all existing silver. The lowest denomination paper money is one peso. An order was also issued this morning establishing a coin reserve system to replace the Bank of Mexico's reserve. (National Telegram, 27th)

Issuance of Small Denomination Paper Subsidiary Currency

Mexico City: After ordering the recall of silver coins circulating in the market yesterday, the government announced that it would issue small denomination paper notes of one peso each to supplement the currently circulating paper money. It is now expected that the exchange rate of pesos to U.S. dollars will be set at a new price of 3.5 pesos per U.S. dollar. It is said that the government's decision was forced by the soaring silver prices caused by the U.S. silver policy. (Reuters, 28th)

Preventing Speculative Profiteering

Mexico City: President General Cárdenas recently issued a proclamation to the people, stating that after the rise in silver prices, speculative behavior immediately followed. The government, in order to curb this, had no choice but to recall hard currency and replace it with paper money. However, if speculators try to take advantage of the situation to profit, the government will deal with them severely and without hesitation. He hopes that the people of the whole country will cooperate with the government so that such severe measures can be avoided. (Havas, 27th)

Silver Price Falls Four Points

(Washington) The price set by the Treasury Department for purchasing silver will not change before Sunday. In the markets of Montreal, Canada, and New York, the price of silver has already fallen four points compared to yesterday due to the unpredictable actions of the U.S. government. At this time, the amount purchased by the government is very small. (Havas, 27th)

Impact on Japan

(Tokyo) As for the impact on Japan of China effectively banning silver exports, Deputy Governor of the Bank of Japan, Fukai, told reporters, "The extent to which China has actually banned silver exports is still unclear, so it is not possible to clearly state the precise impact. However, it would be premature to say that banning silver exports will immediately have a major impact on Japan's trade with China. The question is what the general trend in the Chinese financial world will be after the ban. If the financial world is stable, there will be no problem; otherwise, we must consider the impact on Japan." (Dentsu, 28th)

(Tokyo) If the United States does not change its silver purchase policy, China's financial world will inevitably fall into a chaotic breakdown, which is undoubtedly true. As a result, Japan's trade with China will be affected, but there are optimistic and pessimistic views on the impact. Pessimists say that if China's financial world breaks down, China's purchasing power will decline, which will deal a fatal blow to trade with China, which is expected to improve this year. Since the United States raised silver prices in mid-month, the number of export transactions to China in the Kansai region has already declined sharply. Therefore, it cannot be said that China's financial breakdown has no impact on trade. Optimists say that even if China's financial world breaks down, from an overall point of view, it is only a breakdown of the Shanghai financial world, and it has nothing to do with the purchasing power of inland China. In particular, the recent increase in Japan's exports to China is for necessities. Therefore, due to the exchange rate relationship, Japanese goods, which are internationally in a favorable position, should not be affected by exports to China. (Dentsu, 28th)
