Records of a Northwestern Inspection Tour 89

— Special Correspondent for this Newspaper, Geng Ya

A Glimpse of the Governance and Customs of Chang'an County

Chang'an is the premier county in Guanzhong, bordering Lan to the east, Kun and Xianyang to the west, with the Qinling Mountains to the south, and the Wei and Jing Rivers to the north. It covers an area of approximately sixty to seventy li from east to west and over a hundred li from north to south, totaling more than six thousand square li. Excluding the urban area (Xijing City), the county government's survey report from the twentieth year of the Republic (1931) indicated a rural population of over 280,000. Recent reorganization of the Baojia system and a more detailed survey revealed 65,220 households with a population of 444,530, with males outnumbering females at a ratio of six to four. The population density is approximately forty-six to forty-seven people per square li. The substantial population increase in the county within three years suggests inaccuracies in previous surveys, but it can also be interpreted as a sign of Chang'an's future development. According to County Magistrate Weng Cheng, the county's various conditions are as follows:

Changyi County has an area of over six thousand square li, equivalent to approximately three million mu. However, only 27,572 mu are cultivated as paddy fields and 1,692,785 mu as dry land, totaling 1,730,457 mu. These are the lands subject to grain tax. The remainder is uncultivated or mountainous land, but reclamation and afforestation are possible. The grain tax levy ranges from 2.2 to over 3.4 jiao per mu for civilian land (ordinary people's land), 2.5 to 5.4 jiao for military land (land for supporting the military), and 6.5 jiao to 1.6 yuan for royal land (reclaimed wasteland). The annual tax collection reaches several hundred and forty-three thousand yuan. After deducting grain taxes lost due to floods and the occupation of farmland by highways, the actual revenue is approximately four million two hundred thousand yuan. In addition, miscellaneous tax revenues, such as deed tax, brokerage tax, local tax funds, urban slaughter and transaction tax, and rural livestock slaughter and transaction tax, total around two hundred thousand yuan.

The county's primary education consists of twenty-four county-run schools, including twenty-five senior primary grades and eighty-three junior primary grades, with a total of 4,337 students. There are thirteen private schools, with 2,863 students in senior and junior grades. Additionally, there are 353 private tutorial schools that have been converted into junior primary schools but are not yet officially registered, with 8,658 students. In total, there are 390 schools with 15,858 students, including 14,395 male students and 1,463 female students. The annual expenditure is 87,268 yuan. (Note: Comparing the total number of students in the county to the total population, on average, only one in thirty-six or thirty-seven people is a school-aged child, indicating that school education still needs to be promoted.) In terms of social education, there is one existing public education center and a public reading room attached to the county government building.

Since ancient times, Chang'an has been a battlefield. Distant events such as the Yellow Turban Rebellion, the Five Barbarians Uprising, and the rebellions of Huang Chao and Li Zicheng all ravaged the area. More recently, the Muslim rebellion at the end of the Qing dynasty, the southward crossing of Zhang Yian's Jingguo Army, and Yang Hucheng's defense with the National Revolutionary Army all led to the suburbs of Chang'an becoming battlefields due to the easy access and lack of defensible terrain. The current county jurisdiction has four guard corps, divided into twelve squads, totaling ninety-six guardsmen. The annual expenditure is over eighteen thousand yuan. The corps are stationed in Yinjiahui, Sanqiao, Xinzhu, and Doumen towns, and are equipped with telephone communication, enabling timely information dissemination and ensuring peace and security in the region.

The majority of the people are engaged in agriculture, followed by commerce. Industry is not emphasized. No factories are established in the urban and rural areas. Only in Beizhang Village in the 35th district are people engaged in the traditional manufacture of straw paper and hemp paper. In the 6th district, some are engaged in weaving various bamboo implements. Residents near the mountains engage in firewood gathering and charcoal burning during the agricultural off-season, but the labor is intensive with little profit. The main agricultural product is wheat. Rice is mainly produced in areas bordering the Nanshan Mountains in Hu County. Opium production was very high in previous years. Since the beginning of last spring, an order was issued to prohibit the planting of opium seedlings, and the order was strictly enforced. Over a period of three months, the cleanup was completed. More than one hundred thousand mu of opium seedlings were eradicated. Although there were previous prohibitions, the people regarded them as mere formalities due to the repeated cycles of prohibition and relaxation. As a result, this eradication involved such a large area. Landowners who had their opium crops eradicated were given cotton seeds to plant as compensation. Nineteen cotton production cooperatives, eleven cotton production and marketing cooperatives, four agricultural production cooperatives, and forty-two credit cooperatives were established. Loans totaling more than two hundred thousand yuan were obtained from the Bank of China, Shanghai Bank, Shaanxi Provincial Bank, and other banks. The banks lend to the cooperatives at a monthly interest rate of eight li, and the cooperatives lend to their members and farmers at a rate of twelve li. The four li profit is allocated as follows: 20% for the cooperative's public reserve fund, 20% for the operational staff's compensation, and the remainder for the cooperative's compulsory education fund. Pig farming is the main source of farmers' side income. The director of the public education center, Yang Xingrong, has purchased several Berkshire pigs from Ding County to improve the pig breeds and promote breeding. Many poor rural women work as domestic servants in wealthy households, known locally as "shang zao" (tending the stove), or are hired for long-term employment, known as "la chang gong" (pulling long labor). The employers provide them with coarse food and lodging, and they earn only five or six yuan per year, making their lives quite difficult.

Land ownership in the various villages is not very concentrated. Both public and private entities exercise land rights within the bounds of the law. Tenant farmers have perpetual tenancy rights but no freedom to sell. Land prices have recently been rising due to improved transportation and the completion of various canals. Land near the railway station, which previously cost forty or fifty yuan per mu, has now risen to around two thousand yuan. Government land is divided into three grades, with the highest selling price reaching eighteen hundred yuan. Large family systems are still very common in the villages. The concept of five generations living under one roof and clan support are considered praiseworthy. Families have heads, and clans have elders. Most matters, large and small, are decided by the family or clan head. Small family systems are only found in the cities.

Entertainment organizations include the People's Drama Troupe under the county party headquarters, and ancient music societies in the city organize ancient music performances every June. There are also the Xijing Epigraphy and Calligraphy Exhibition and the Xijing Painting and Calligraphy Association, which are open to visitors at any time to cultivate the public's aesthetic interests. Social drama troupes include the Yisu, Sanyi, Zhengsu, and Youmin Qinqiang opera troupes, and the Xin Wutai Beijing opera troupe. There are also the Afanggong and Xijing Cinemas. However, these are all located in the city. In the villages, old-style plays are occasionally performed on earthen stages.

The urban area is a mix of people from different places with diverse dialects. The basic local dialect pronounces "shu" (comb) and "shu" (book) as "fu," "rou" (meat) as "wu," "shui" (water) as "fei," "zamen" (we) as "zaimen," and "anmen" (we) as "men." "Bi" (pen) is called "shenghuo" (living), (as it is in Lanzhou). "Mianbao" (bread) is called "momo." "Moving slowly" is called "mu lang," "not conforming to the crowd" is called "ning ci," "stirring up trouble" is called "shan yin huo," "unclean" is called "wo nang," "arrogant" is called "pin ma," "keeping secrets" is called "nie zhu," "destroying" is called "shi chang," and "beautiful" is called "liao bao bao." In the poem "Jiao ren liao xi," the commentary explains that "liao" means "good," which is also an ancient Zhou and Qin pronunciation.

Jiangxi Remnant Bandits Can Be Quickly Eliminated 90

—District Commanders Are Actively Searching and Suppressing—

Nanchang dispatch: Last year, when the bandit leaders Zhu De and Mao Zedong led their main force of the false central army to flee far into Sichuan, Hunan, Guangxi, and Guizhou, they left the bandit leaders Ye Jianying and Chen Yi to collect the remnants in southern Jiangxi, attempting a final struggle. Currently, the newly recovered districts have been divided into areas by the pacification office to establish Pacification Commanders, responsible for searching and suppressing remnant bandits, attracting back refugees, providing disaster relief, restoring order, and organizing self-defense, with the aim of achieving stability. Remnant bandits in the hinterland of Jiangxi Province have been largely eliminated, and highways and Baojia systems have been completed successively. However, the factions led by Ye Jianying in the Huichang and Yudu areas, and Chen Yi in the Yongfeng, Jishui, and Wujiang areas, are still fleeing east and west. Furthermore, the remaining evils of the Fang bandits in northeastern Jiangxi and the borders of Fujian, Zhejiang, and Anhui, such as Shao Shiping and Zou Qi, and the bandits led by Cai Huiwen in the border areas of Jiangxi, Hubei, and Hunan, as well as small groups of scattered bandits in various places that had been deeply affected by banditry in the past, cannot be eradicated immediately. The pacification office has ordered the district commanders to continue to blockade, encircle, and search for them. Recently, local troops stationed there have been engaged in suppression and pacification, and have made every effort to set up blockades and pillboxes. These remnant bandits have lost their ability to rally support, but the bandits who are coerced and oppressed by the bandit leaders have no way to break free from their shackles to start anew. However, their complete elimination is only a matter of time. (26th)

Building a Dike at the Mouth of the Yellow River 91

Preparations are complete, construction to begin on May 1st, the Yellow River-Grand Canal combined shipping to be realized this autumn

Jinan Dispatch: Director of the Department of Construction, Zhang Honglie, led Zhao Weihan, head of the department's section, Secretary Wang Zhigang, Technician Shi Andong, and Hu Xueli from the Long-Distance Telephone Administration Office, departed from Jinan on the 20th of this month to inspect the diligence of government officials in northern Shandong, convene the Public Security Bureau's Lian Zhuang Hui for roll call and instruction, and inspect the achievements of the fourth and fifth departments, long-distance telephone and tree planting, etc. After passing through fifteen counties including Lijin, Zhanhua, Wudi, Yangxin, Huimin, Shanghe, Linyi, Yucheng, Gaotang, Boping, Liaocheng, Linqing, Xialü, Enxian, and Pingyuan, on the evening of the 26th, they returned to Jinan by special train. According to Zhang, "I first went to Lijin to see the Yellow River silted wasteland. In addition to the designated reclamation area that can accommodate 7,000 disaster victims, a section was also designated in Machang that can accommodate 200 people. The disaster victims in western Shandong have all arrived in the reclamation area and have been properly settled. Each person lives in a shack, and land has been allocated, 50 mu per person. They are now engaged in reclamation. The Yellow River silted land is all fertile farmland, but the lack of rain this spring is quite dry. From Lijin to Haikou, there are about 200 li. I inspected the area 130 or 140 li from Lijin. In the first half of the section, I often saw the small houses of the original reclamation residents, because the former reclamation residents went home after the harvest and did not live here, so the houses were simply built and could only last for a year. The second half of the section was uninhabited because it was far from Haikou and difficult to travel. If I went further down, it would take four or five days to return, so I did not go to Haikou to save time. As for the problem of building a dike at the mouth of the river and blocking the Luan Jing Zi branch ditch, the people of Lijin County shirked responsibility to the disaster victims who moved there for reclamation, and the construction was delayed. Now it has been completely resolved. Lijin allocates labor to cooperate with the disaster victims, and the disaster victims are responsible for more, and the people of Lijin County are responsible for less, in order to complete it. The materials have been prepared, and construction will begin uniformly on May 1st. The measurement team previously sent by the Department of Construction and the River Affairs Bureau measured Haikou, starting from Lijin across the river and measuring from Zhanhua on the south bank. Now it has been completed in most cases. The dike construction project requires a total of 300,000 square feet of labor. 20,000 yuan of construction funds have been allocated. Those who are responsible for building the dike are given a subsidy of 2 jiao per cubic foot of earth. After the Yellow River project Guan Tai blocked the mouth, the silt was not greatly affected, so the river level was stable. After I finished inspecting northern Shandong, I went west and inspected the Grand Canal when I passed Liaocheng and Linqing. The Northern Canal navigation plan has long been completed, requiring a total of 370,000 yuan of construction funds. The central government has agreed to allocate 260,000 yuan. In the next two months, 80,000 yuan can be received first. After receiving it, we will first start with important places. The combined shipping of the Yellow River and the Grand Canal can be realized in July or August of this year. The section from Linqing to Tianjin can still be navigable, but the water volume is too small, and only the smallest boats can travel back and forth. The water volume of the Grand Canal must be increased before larger boats can pass, which will facilitate merchants. The general situation of the counties I inspected this time is very good. Each county has planted many trees this spring. The Huimin Automobile Road has planted 40 or 50 li of new roadside trees this year, which are willow trees and have all survived. They are all trimmed neatly. There is a section of Qingping's flower arrangement land between Gaotang and Boping, which is 12 li long. The poplar trees planted last year and the year before last have all survived and are now 3 feet high and very neat and lush. The Lian Zhuang Hui in Yucheng trained for 70 days, and the results were very good. The Lian Zhuang Hui in Pingyuan, which has only been training for 40 days, is in even better condition. The county's Public Security Bureau is also very good. The inspection situation in each county passed on this trip will be made into a general report for comparison, etc. (27th)

An Overview of the Implementation of the Guide-Huai Project 92

Divided into several items such as dredging, building dikes, and building gates

Beijing News: The purpose of the Guide-Huai Plan is to prevent floods, facilitate shipping, promote irrigation, eliminate harm, and promote benefits, while considering both. All the plans have been studied and stipulated in detail, and have been submitted to the National Government for approval. In recent years, the Guide-Huai Committee has implemented the most urgent and effective projects within its financial capacity. The following is a brief description of the projects that have been built and are underway.

(1) Preliminary Dredging Project of the Zhangfu River: The Zhangfu River is the first section of the sea-bound waterway in the flood discharge project, and it is also the main channel for diverting water from the Huai River to the Grand Canal in the irrigation and shipping projects. It starts from Gaoliangjian at the mouth of Hongze Lake and ends at Matouzhen, the entrance to the canal, with a total length of about 31 kilometers. It has been in disrepair for many years, and the siltation is increasing day by day. The Guide-Huai Committee started construction in January of the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), widening and deepening the original river channel. It was completed in July, requiring a total of more than 470,000 yuan. After the completion of the project, shipping, which used to be dry and shallow, is now smooth and unobstructed. In addition, last year, various places suffered from severe drought, but the canal area relied entirely on the dredging of this river to provide abundant water. Because of this, the eastern part of the Jiangbei Canal was greatly irrigated. On the 14th of this month, the members of the Guide-Huai Committee went to Huaiyin to inspect the ship lock project and took a boat through the Zhangchen River to visit the Honghu Dam. They inspected along the river and saw that the river surface was wide, and the water depth was sufficient. The Huai River from the upper reaches discharged from Hongze Lake, passing through the lower reaches of the river and coming directly to the canal, with a very smooth flow. This is enough to prove that the initial Guide-Huai project of the Guide-Huai Committee has been completed with limited costs and has achieved remarkable results.

(2) Building Shaobo, Huaiyin, and Liujian Ship Locks: The Grand Canal runs vertically through the north and south of Jiangsu Province, and it is an important channel for irrigation and navigation in the lower reaches of the Huai River. However, its water potential fluctuates with the seasons. When it is flooded, it overflows, and when it is dry, it dries up. Although there is a canal, it cannot be used to its full extent. To maximize the use of the canal, its water level must be maintained at a considerable height, with little change throughout the winter and summer. Major ships can pass smoothly all year round, and the counties in eastern Shandong can also benefit from irrigation. In the middle of the canal, there were many old stone gates, which were all built across the river, leaving a two-zhang wide opening for ships to pass through. Every time ships pass through the gate, they have to be dragged by a winch, which is dangerous and time-consuming. Moreover, the water flow through the gate is often continuous day and night, with no way to regulate the discharge. The Guide-Huai Committee, in order to improve the current situation of the canal, established three ship lock engineering bureaus in Shaobo, Huaiyin, and Liurun in the 23rd year of the Republic (1934) and built a new-style ship lock in each place. The lock chamber of the ship lock is 100 meters long and 10 meters wide, and its capacity is enough to allow one 900-ton ship or ten 40-ton ships to pass through the lock at one time. The gate is made of steel, and the lock wall is made of steel-reinforced concrete. Both sides of the lock chamber are paved with stone blocks and built as slopes. There are also water pipes placed on both sides of the bottom of the lock chamber, connecting the upper and lower gates, and there are opening and closing machines on both sides of the gate, which are very convenient to use. The maximum water level difference between the upstream and downstream of the gate is 7.7 meters at the Shaobo Gate and 9.2 meters at the Huaiyin and Liujian Gates. The cost of each ship lock, including materials, is about 600,000 yuan. In order to facilitate construction and not interfere with the current traffic on the canal, they are all built on the land of the river bay, and diversion canals are dug to connect the canal, and then the foundation piling project is implemented. To date, the diversion canals in the three places have been completed. The large and small piles and steel sheet piles of the lower foundation of the water channel on both sides of the upstream and downstream of the Shaobo and Huaiyin gates have also been completed. They are now rushing to assemble the steel bars and engage in concrete work, working day and night. It is expected that the work can be completed by the end of June this year. As for the Liujian Ship Lock, the foundation piling project is being actively carried out, and it will also be completed in August of this year. After the completion of the three gates, the water potential of the canal can be maintained at a considerable depth throughout the year. From Sanjiangying in the Yangtze River, along the canal to the Yunhe Station north of the intersection of the Longhai Railway, a total of 350 kilometers, ships with a draft of 2 meters and a load of 900 tons can pass unobstructed. The important towns along the way, such as Shaobo, Gaoyou, Bao Ying, Huai'an, Huaiyin, and Suqian, are all prosperous areas in northern Jiangsu. The development of transportation in the future can be predicted.

(3) Organizing the East and West Banks of the Grand Canal: The east bank of the Grand Canal has been in disrepair for many years, and now the Jiangsu Provincial Grand Canal Engineering Bureau is raising and thickening it, dismantling the old sweep, or paving stone work to protect it. There are more than 20 culvert breaches on the west bank, which must be repaired separately or fitted with cave doors to maintain the water level of the Grand Canal and manipulate the water flow. The project is handled by the Shaobo Ship Lock Engineering Bureau of the Guide-Huai Committee. Three engineering offices are set up in Bao Ying Gaoyou Zhaoguan Dam to start construction at the same time on the entire line. Some have been completed, and some are being filled and repaired. It is expected that they can be completed before June.

(4) Building the Gaoyou Small Ship Lock: The Gaoyou Yuehe Port on the west bank of the Grand Canal is an important channel for ships in Gaobao Lake to enter the Grand Canal. The Guide-Huai Committee plans to build a small ship lock there to facilitate transportation. The port will be closed after the construction of the small ship lock begins. It is currently being prepared and will begin construction soon.

(5) Repairing the Huiji Dam: The Huiji Dam in Matouzhen of the Grand Canal is the outlet of the newly dredged Zhangfu River. It is urgent to rebuild and install active gates to manipulate the irrigation water volume and navigation water level in the canal. The Guide-Huai Committee has prepared the project and will start construction immediately.

(6) Building the Sanhe Active Dam: Hongze Lake has the function of absorbing and discharging the Huai River, but the method of controlling the water volume has only been to build a temporary grass dam in Jiangba. This grass dam is used to bind reeds into a sweep on the lakeside to resist lake waves, and then add soil to prevent leakage. For the convenience of closure, the dam is only repaired and blocked when the Hongze Lake water level is too low. However, the grass dam is light, and it is washed away when the water rises the following spring. It cannot be controlled according to the season. If the Huai flood rises, the lake water overflows the embankment, and the obstruction of the dam base and dam head to the water flow prevents the lake water from being discharged smoothly. The Guide-Huai Committee therefore plans to build a new-style active dam with a total length of 60 holes, each 10 meters wide and 5.5 meters high. The foundation and piers are all built with concrete, and the doors are made of steel, each of which can move freely and open and close freely, requiring about 3.5 million yuan in construction costs. The dam is built on the land south of the Sanhekou, and diversion canals are dug to connect Hongze Lake and the Sanhe River. The project of excavating the diversion canals has been tendered this spring, requiring a price of more than 1.7 million yuan. The Guide-Huai Committee has set up a Sanhe Active Dam Engineering Bureau there and has started construction. After the success of the dam, the lake water can be pre-discharged during floods to wait for the accumulation of floodwater, and the lake water can be pre-regulated during droughts to provide irrigation and navigation water sources. Large ships with a draft of 2 meters can enter Sanjiangying from the Yangtze River, pass through the Shaobo and Huaiyin ship locks, exit the Zhangfu River and pass through Hongze Lake, and reach Bengbu and Huaiyuan in the west. In peacetime, the lake water can be blocked, so that it can enter the sea waterway through the Zhangfu River and return to the sea, so that the sea waterway can be scoured for a long time and become deeper day by day. Therefore, the active dam is the main key to the separation of the river and the sea and the irrigation and navigation plan, and it cannot be delayed. It is expected that it will be completed in two years.

(7) Building the Yangzhuang Active Dam: The Guide-Huai Plan has decided on the principle of separating the river and the sea. There is already a project to build a Sanhe Active Dam at the Sanhekou of the Jiang River waterway to regulate discharge, and it has also been decided to build an active dam at Yangzhuang on the sea waterway. Its effect is the same as that of the Sanhe Active Dam. It is currently being planned and prepared, and it can be tendered next month.

(8) Building the Yankou Ship Lock: The Yankou River is an important channel for connecting Huaihai traffic. However, there is no direct navigation between the Yankou River and the Grand Canal. Goods coming from the Yankou River must first be discharged at the West Dam and transferred to boats, barged for more than ten miles through the abandoned Yellow River, and then transferred to boats again to reach the Grand Canal, which is very inconvenient. The Guide-Huai Committee plans to build a new-style ship lock near Yangzhuang to allow direct navigation between the Yankou and Grand Canal. As for the design of the ship lock, it is similar to the one built in Huaiyin. As soon as the Huaiyin Ship Lock is completed, it can be continued.

(9) Building the Liulaojian Water Discharge Gate: The Yi River contains a lot of sediment, and it detours through the Middle Grand Canal, carrying sediment south, which is very harmful to the downstream. In order to prevent and block it, the Guide-Huai Committee has built a ship lock at Liulaojian to block its muddy water from going south. The Jiangsu Provincial Government has also completed the reorganization of the Liutang River, the main channel for the Yi River to return to the sea. Therefore, the construction of a new water discharge gate between the Liutang River and the Grand Canal is necessary. According to Liulaojian, there used to be a nine-hole gate for discharging Yi River into Liutang River. Later, it was changed to a rolling dam. After the dam collapsed, grass dams were used to start and block every year, but it still could not fully store and discharge water. It is now planned to build a new-style water discharge gate upstream of the Liurun Ship Lock, with a total length of 10 holes and a discharge capacity of 1,000 cubic meters. After the Liulaojian Ship Lock is completed, it will be started.

(10) Guide the Water into the Sea Project: The Huai River has only two outlets, the Jiang River and the sea. However, if all of it enters the Jiang River, the Jiang River may not be able to handle it. If all of it enters the sea, the construction cost is huge and does not conform to economic principles. After weighing the pros and cons and studying the gains and losses in detail, it was decided to adopt the principle of separating the Jiang and the sea. The sea waterway runs from Zhangfu River through the abandoned Yellow River to the Taizi entrance to enter the sea, with a total length of more than 170 kilometers. The project is huge and difficult. The Guide-Huai Committee negotiated with the Jiangsu Provincial Government and obtained the consent of the provincial government to handle the implementation of the project. Starting from Yangzhuang in the northwest of Huaiyin and ending at Taizi Port in the northeast of Funing, 160,000 workers were recruited to work at the construction site, taking advantage of the agricultural slack time from October to May of the following year to excavate earthwork. The entire project is expected to be completed in May of the 25th year of the Republic (1936).

Ministry of Railways Plan: Construction of the Zhendong Railway 93

Abstract of the Survey Report

Zhenjiang News: Previously, people from Jiangsu Province suggested to the Ministry of Railways to construct a railway from Kouan to Dongtai (East Taizhou). The Ministry of Railways sent personnel to survey the area. The Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce, considering Kou-Dong Railway's isolated position, proposed the idea of constructing the Zhen-Dong Railway last month, requesting the Ministry of Railways to change the route. The ministry sent personnel to survey again, and the result was that a change was indeed necessary. They are now actively proceeding with it, hoping to realize it soon. The surveyor also drafted a survey report, divided into ten chapters: 1. General Discussion; 2. Comparison of Constructing the Kou-Dong Railway and the Zhen-Dong Railway; 3. The Topography and Economic Overview of the Lixiahe Region; 4. The Transportation Situation in the Lixiahe Region and a Comparison of Water and Land Transportation; 5. The Plan for the New Reclamation Area in the Lixiahe Region and its Relationship with the Railway; 6. The Situation of Salt Production in Huainan and its Relationship with the Railway; 7. The Route and Engineering Plan of the Zhen-Dong Railway; 8. The Arrangement of Zhenjiang Wharf and the Regulations on Ferry Fees; 9. Engineering Budget of the Zhen-Dong Railway and Forecast of Passenger and Freight Transportation and Operating Expenses; 10. Conclusion. The report is over 20,000 words long. An abstract is recorded as follows:

General Survey: People from Jiangsu Province, recognizing the importance of transportation in the Lixiahe region, proposed building the Kou-Dong Railway, starting from Kouan, passing through Taixian, to Dongtai, with a total length of 80 kilometers and a construction cost of 3 million yuan, predicting a surplus of over 500,000 yuan. Based on this survey, it is believed that the dense population and abundant agricultural products in the Lixiahe region necessitate the construction of a railway. Moreover, the construction of a railway is particularly important to promote the new reclamation area plan. However, the Kou-Dong route is isolated and difficult to develop in the future, and it will greatly affect the business of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway. Therefore, while surveying the Kou-Dong route, a line from Zhenjiang to Taixian was surveyed separately, and the Zhen-Dong Railway plan was drafted for comparison. This line starts from Qihaokou on the opposite bank of Zhenjiang, passes through Jiangdu Xiannv Temple, Taixian, to Dongtai, with a length of 128 kilometers, an estimated construction cost of 4.53 million yuan, and can be completed in two years. The predicted income is 1,337,000 yuan, operating expenses are 572,800 yuan, interest is 162,000 yuan, and the surplus is about 402,200 yuan. With this plan, it can connect with the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, cultivate each other, and prosper Zhenjiang and Jiangdu. If, after the completion of the entire line, it is extended northward from Dongtai to Yancheng or Daning, the business will undoubtedly see development.

Comparison of the Two Routes: Northern Jiangsu, east from the East China Sea and west to the Grand Canal, north to the Yellow River diversion area, and south to the Yangtze River, including Funing, Yancheng, Dongtai, Taixian, and Xinghua counties, is collectively called Lixiahe. Because transportation on the east, west, and north sides is inconvenient, the three ports along the Yangtze River, Huojiaqiao, Kouan, and Tianshenggang, serve as its gateways. All Yangtze River steamships stop here for connection. The route from Tianshenggang to Dongtai is the Tongyu Railway. There is no need to discuss this line further. Huojiaqiao is located in Jiangdu, with the same position as Qihaokou. The comparison between the Kou-Dong and Zhen-Dong railways is as follows: (1) The Kou-Dong Railway is only 80 kilometers long. Its southern end from Kouan to Danyang is 50 kilometers, and its northern end from Dongtai to Haizhou is 270 kilometers. The route itself is very short and isolated. It is better to change the route through Jiangdu to Qihaokou on the opposite bank of Zhenjiang, connecting with the Beijing-Shanghai Railway across the river and serving as a cultivating line for Beijing-Shanghai. (2) Zhenjiang is the capital of Jiangsu Province and a major port on the Yangtze River. The Jiangbei Railway should connect here, which can benefit from commercial transportation and achieve military and political control. Therefore, the Kou-Dong route should be abandoned in favor of the Zhen-Dong route. (3) The Beijing-Shanghai Railway connects to Jinpu in the north, Jingwu in the south, and Huhangyonghangjiang and other lines in the east, stretching for thousands of miles. Although the Zhen-Dong Railway is on the opposite bank, it can connect with the existing railways and avoid the isolated position of the Kou-Dong Railway. (4) If the Zhen-Dong Railway extends westward from Jiangdu, passing through Yiwei, Liuhe, to Pukou, it will connect with the Jinpu Railway. It can connect with various routes in North China and use the capital's ferry to connect with various routes in Jiangnan. Although the Jiangdu-Pukou line is parallel to the Yangtze River, it is quite important militarily and there is a possibility of construction in the future. (5) Jiangdu is a major city in Jiangbei, located at the mouth of the Grand Canal into the Yangtze River. The Customs used to consider its location superior, but since the construction of the Jinpu Railway, commerce has declined. If the Kou-Dong Railway is built, Zhenjiang and Jiangdu will decline further. Therefore, changing the railway route, passing through Jiangdu to Qihaokou, not only restores the prosperity of Zhenjiang and Jiangdu, but also uses the existing prosperity of the two ports to assist the railway's business. (6) Currently, much of the transportation in Lixiahe passes through Zhenjiang, transferring to the Beijing-Shanghai Railway to reach various ports. If the Kou-Dong Railway is built, the connection between Kouan and other ports will rely on water transportation, which will take away the original business of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway. Therefore, it is proposed to change the route to the north bank of Zhenjiang and absorb water transportation.

Zhen-Dong Route: The Zhen-Dong railway line is planned to start from Qihaokou on the opposite bank of Zhenjiang, where a ferry pier will be built for docking. The station facilities will be simple. From here, the route goes north to Jiangdu Station in the southeast of Jiangdu City. The southeast sides of Jiangdu County are adjacent to the Grand Canal, and the ferry terminals are all outside Fuyun Gate. Crossing the ferry south from Fuyun Gate is the terminal of the Zhenyang Automobile Company. About half a mile to the west, a railway bridge is currently under construction and will be completed soon. In the future, railway passengers can enter the city via this bridge. After the railway leaves Jiangdu Station, it goes northeast and then east, passing through Wanfu Bridge (457 meters), Shiyanggou Bridge (181 meters), Dongjia Bridge (818 meters), and Qizha Bridge (approximately 67 meters), a total of five bridges to Xiannv Temple. The total length of the five bridges is 833 meters. Except for the Shiyanggou Bridge, where the clearance from the water surface should be 9 meters for navigation, the remaining bridges are not navigable. If the section is changed to pass through Yanjiaqiao and Xiaobaidu, only two bridges need to be built, with a total length of 753 meters, but Yanjiaqiao must be raised to facilitate navigation. These two lines should be carefully compared in the future for selection. After the route leaves Xiannv Temple, it follows the banks of the Tongyang Canal, passing through Yiling to Taixian City. The prosperous commercial area and ferry terminals of Taixian are all located in the north of the city. The terminals are divided into Shangheba and Xiaheba. All steamships docking upstream from Taixian to the Yangtze River use the Shanghe terminal, and all steamships docking downstream from Taixian to Dongtai and Xinghua use the Xiahe terminal. Shanghe and Xiahe can originally communicate with each other, but because the waterway passes through the city, it has gradually been silted up by residents, and over time, they have become isolated. Therefore, passenger and freight transport must be transferred at this dam. This is a major obstacle to transportation in Lixiahe. Due to the terrain, the railway station is located in the city. The route crosses the Tongyang Canal in Taixian, going east along its north bank, passing through Jiangyan and then turning north, passing through Liujiadun, Zhoujiashe, to Jiajialou in Shihuai East. Although this section of the route is slightly longer than the line going southeast from Taixian, passing through Lijiapu, Xiazhushe, Shujiashe, to Jiajialou, its terrain is higher and it passes through the large towns of Jiangyan and Shiyan, which are its advantages and can be compared in the future. After the route leaves Jijialou, it goes north-eastward along the east bank of the Yanyun Canal, directly to the south of Dongtai County, where Dongtai Station will be built. If it is planned to extend to Yancheng in the future, it can be extended northward from here.

Passenger and Freight Transportation: The Zhen-Dong route does not connect with the existing railways. If narrow-gauge railways are built to save costs, it is also possible. However, for future development, a broad-gauge plan is tentatively proposed, with a construction cost of 4.53 million yuan. The prediction of passenger and freight transportation is extremely difficult. Based on the current water transportation situation, it is estimated that the railway passenger transport can reach approximately 89,000,000 passenger-kilometers. The current ticket price for Zhenyang automobiles is one yuan per passenger, and two jiao per passenger is sufficient if the railway is available. Assuming that 6,220,000 passenger-kilometers can be obtained throughout the year, the total is 95,120,000 kilometers. Among this total, assuming that one-third are fourth-class passengers, calculated at 6 li per person per kilometer, the fare income would be 190,000 yuan. Two-thirds are third-class passengers, calculated at 1 fen per person per kilometer, the fare income would be 634,000 yuan. The total passenger ticket income is approximately 824,000 yuan. Freight transport is estimated to be approximately 61,870,000 ton-kilometers for the entire route, calculated at 8 li 3 hao per ton per kilometer, which would yield 513,000 yuan. The total annual income from passenger and freight transport is 1,337,000 yuan.

Survey Conclusion: The economic situation and engineering overview of the Zhen-Dong Railway have been described above. However, due to the rushed survey, it is not entirely accurate, which is a concern. Moreover, this survey did not carry instruments for terrain measurement because the area is flat and has no mountains. Furthermore, the Jiangsu Provincial Construction Department has 10,000 copies of measured maps for design, which are more than accurate enough. Although the two items of passenger and freight income and operating expenses are not guaranteed to match the actual situation, they are analyzed item by item so that auditors have a basis for supplementing and revising them, and it is not difficult to obtain accurate results. If this transportation forecast is not inconsistent with future operating income, the railway's own economy, in addition to paying interest, can still repay 400,000 yuan per year. Even if the estimated amount exceeds the actual start of traffic and fails to repay the debt according to the amount, the government still has a necessity to construct the railway for the sake of transportation in Lixiahe and the development of the region's economy. Moreover, the construction of this route is actually a cultivating line for the Beijing-Shanghai Railway. It is estimated that the Beijing-Shanghai Railway can increase passenger transport by 158,000,000 passenger-kilometers and freight transport by 66,000,000 ton-kilometers per year. The combined income of these two items is no less than one million yuan. Therefore, the construction of the Zhen-Dong Railway, although its own benefits are small, its benefits to society and the cultivation of Beijing-Shanghai's business are great.

National Woodcut Exhibition Opens in Jinan 94

—Over a Thousand Works—

Jinan Correspondence: Jin Zhaoye and others collected woodcut works from all over the country and reference materials from China and abroad, and held a national woodcut exhibition at the YMCA in Jinan. The opening was held today (the 27th). Many people from the art and literature circles visited. The exhibition room is divided into three parts: (1) Modern woodcut works, the largest in number; (2) Ancient woodcut works, including Japanese works and versions, etc., with Ming Dynasty and Qing Dynasty Tongzhi Daoguang versions, paintings of Romance of the Three Kingdoms, Jin Ping Mei, etc.; (3) New Year pictures, also collected in large quantities, allowing a comparison of the past and present. The woodcut knives made by Wang Mazi Iron Shop in Beijing have contributed greatly to the art of woodcut in recent years. The association also has a set on public display. Among the works, Li Hua's "Galloping Horse" is swift and vigorous, with the spirit of a horse neighing in the wind, and Luo Qingzhen's "Landscape" is meticulous and elegant. Gu Gan's "Night of September 18th" depicts the scene of Shenyang city in the hazy night, with fires illuminating the sky, and the military and civilians fleeing in panic. The sound of cannons and cries can be heard. Although it is a moment of extreme chaos, it is vividly depicted. Liu Yan's "Girl" and "Landscape" are lifelike and very poetic. The most poetic is Zhang Hui's "The Moon is Full, but the Person is Not," depicting a woman leaning on a railing outside a small pavilion, her sleeves cold, looking at the moon with sorrow. Wang Shaoluo's "The Moon Rises on the Willow Branch" depicts a desolate moonlight scene, similar to the previous picture, with willows swaying and a person standing alone in an empty courtyard, admiring his own shadow, just at the time of a rendezvous after dusk. The number of works is about a thousand. (27th)

Songjiang: Wage Dispute Among River Dredging Workers 95

The county is dredging the city moat. The first section has been inspected and accepted by the Provincial Committee in Songjiang. The fifth section, from Waiguan驿 outside the West Gate to Baojia Bridge, has already started construction. The project is contracted by Cao Xinquan from Ningbo. Pan Binglin from Tiantai, Zhejiang, sub-contracted a part of the work from Cao. There were 55 workers. After Pan received the wages from Cao, he did not distribute them to the workers. Because of the wage dispute, the workers went on strike. Fearing that it would affect the entire project, Cao urgently sought a solution, paid off the wages, including the four days of the strike. After deducting what Pan had already received, he found more than 70 yuan and declared dismissal. Twenty of the workers were still willing to work with Cao in Songjiang, but they could not get anything from Pan and turned to Cao for payment. Cao was dragged out of his residence in the Xilin Temple by the workers. Zheng Daquan, a jailer from the county, was from the same hometown as Pan and also negotiated on behalf of the workers. When the crowd passed through the street, the citizens almost thought they had caught an escaped prisoner. Then they went to Wu Zhidao of China-England Pharmacy, Cao's guarantor, but could not find a solution. They went to the district office, where acting district chief Lu mediated and explained that Cao had already paid off the wages and the workers should seek repayment from Pan. He also explained to the jailer Zheng that Ningbo and Tiantai were both from Zhejiang and there was no difference between them, and persuaded them to be kind. However, Cao, the foreman, felt that he had been insulted for no reason and asked the district office to uphold justice. It is unknown how the matter will be resolved.

Wuxi: Improving the Silkworm Seed Control Method 96

The local silkworm seed industry association held a meeting of members yesterday. Representatives from 14 seed fields attended, chaired by Jiang Jiayou. The following important matters were resolved: 1. The spring silkworm industry this year suffered from many malpractices due to the improper control methods of the province. Seed sellers raised seed prices, harming the rearing households. It was decided to request the Jiangsu Provincial Sericulture Improvement Management Committee to make use of the baojia system during the autumn silkworm season to investigate the required number of silkworm seeds from the township heads in advance, and then distribute them to the rearing households, so as to avoid the temporary shortage or surplus. 2. It was requested that the Provincial Sericulture Improvement Association increase the price of autumn seeds by one jiao per sheet. 3. The term of office of the current executive and supervisory committee members has expired. It should be requested that the county party department send personnel to guide the re-election. In addition, the spring silkworms have been harvested in the past two days. The market price of mulberry leaves is two yuan per dan.

Teahouse Gambling Villagers Injure Police and Snatch Criminals 97

The second branch of the Houqiao Public Security Bureau in this county, patrol officer Ma Zemin, received a report the other day that there was a gambling situation in Shengjiaqiao Pu Yinquan Teahouse in the jurisdiction. He immediately sent a police officer to arrest eight gamblers and gambling equipment. Just as he was about to take them to the bureau, villagers suddenly gathered and beat the police officer, snatching six gamblers. Police officer Xu Nianfeng was injured and lost a six-round revolver with five bullets, and a wooden-cased pistol with five bullets. Because they were outnumbered, the police only managed to arrest Pu Jisheng and Pu Zhongyi, two gamblers. After bringing them back to the station, they were taken to the county public security bureau together with the injured policeman. After Zhang, a clerk, opened the court for interrogation, he ordered the injured policeman to submit himself to the court for injury verification, and to detain the gambling criminals Pu Jisheng and Pu Zhongyi. It was scheduled to transfer them to the local branch court today for trial.

Changzhou: Zhenxin Cloth Factory in Dongxiatang Burned Down 98

The Zhenxin Cloth Factory in Dongxiatang, Wuyi, caught fire at about 2:00 AM this morning (28th). Because it was late at night, by the time people in the factory woke up and immediately reported to the fire brigade in each district for rescue, the fire had already spread and its intensity was very high. All the looms and other parts were completely engulfed and burned, resulting in huge losses. After the fire brigade in each district tried their best to put out the fire, it was finally extinguished at dawn.

Jiangyin: Executing Two Children Sentenced to Death 99

Yao Yingsheng, a farmer from Dongzitucun, Shizhuang Town, 7th District, had his two young sons, Jinchang and Fuchang, hacked to death by his neighbor Peng Quanhai with an iron shovel at 3:00 PM on March 31st, due to long standing grudges. After investigation and verification by the county, the murderer was arrested and detained. Yesterday (27th), he was brought to court. After the presiding judges pronounced the verdict, Peng Quanhai was sentenced to death for premeditated murder. If he does not agree, he may appeal to the High Court.

Fish Donation Collected According to Regulations 100

Chen Jingxin, director of the local donation collection office in this county, collected donations for the relief home from various fish shops based on the donation for yellow croakers, etc. The fish industry association had submitted a request to the provincial department for exemption. The finance department previously reported to the county government that this case involved trivial matters and was not suitable for inclusion, ordering the county to comply with the record. County Magistrate Yan believed that the fish donation had been submitted to the 22nd-year budget and instructed by the provincial government that this fish donation subsidy should be changed to a fish industry charity subsidy and collected according to the number. Yesterday (27th), he ordered the local donation collection office to collect and remit the number according to regulations.

Haimen: Dasheng No. 3 Factory Completely Contracts 101

Dasheng No. 3 Factory in this county was founded by Zhang Qian and has been operating prosperously since its opening, with annual surpluses and excellent results. It is a well-known textile factory in China. However, in recent years, due to sluggish market conditions and stagnant sales, it has been losing more than 10,000 yuan per month. If remedies are not sought urgently, it will be difficult to sustain. Therefore, a factory affairs meeting was held yesterday to decide on a complete contraction, laying off redundant staff, saving materials, and reducing more than 40 unnecessary expenses. If the market still shows no signs of improvement, the first step of contraction will be carried out.

Taro Silk Boat Capsizes in the River 102

This county suffered from a prolonged drought last year, and the autumn harvest was sharply reduced. Now, at the time of year when crops have been depleted and next harvest is not yet in, food is in short supply, and people are unusually panicked. Fortunately, the disaster relief committee raised disaster relief funds, purchased taro silk, and held low-priced sales, which helped to maintain the livelihood of the poor. The other day, the committee entrusted a Shanghai merchant, Fang, to purchase 2,400 dans of taro silk and transport it to Haimen. However, when it reached the Nandiangang River surface, it suddenly encountered a strong wind and capsized instantly. The five crew members and the taro silk, etc., all sank into the river and could not be salvaged, resulting in a huge loss.

Nantong: Abundant Coastal Fish Harvest 103

Due to the eradication of sea bandits, a large number of fishing boats went to sea in Jiangbei's coastal areas of Lvsi, Fengli, and Jugang. In the past half month, the fish catches at each port have reached 800,000 yuan. However, the purchasing power of the people during the spring famine is weak, and fish prices are unusually low, with selling prices only half of what they were in previous years.

Striving for Electricity Fee Reduction 104

The electricity fee in Tongcheng is sold at 2 jiao 5 fen per unit. Users claim that the electricity company purchases electricity from the power plant for only 4 and a half fen per unit and demand a reduction to 2 jiao. The two sides refuse to yield to each other. The entire business community automatically stopped using electricity on the 27th, resulting in a dark world. The matter is currently being mediated by the Chamber of Commerce.

Hangzhou: China Bank Clerk Killed While Delivering Money 106

Huang Xikun, a clerk at the Hangzhou Sanyuanfang China Bank, was in his thirties and from Xiaoshan. He had been working at the bank for many years. At 7:00 AM on the 27th, he was carrying more than 7,000 yuan in cash to deliver and receive remittances to various households. Among them was Qian from Shanghai Yipinxing Cai Restaurant, who remitted 140 yuan to Qian's residence at No. 46 Shangcang Bridge. When Huang delivered the money according to the house number, he did not expect that several bandits were lying in ambush in the residence. They rushed out, killed Huang, robbed him of more than 5,000 yuan in cash, and fled. After waiting for Huang for a long time without him returning, the China Bank sent someone to search everywhere in the afternoon but could not find him. This morning (28th), another clerk went to the vicinity of Shangcang Bridge to deliver money and saw a China Bank bicycle parked at the entrance of No. 46. He recognized it as Huang's and went inside to check. He saw that there was no one in the room, but he found Huang Xikun's body lying in a pool of blood. He had a knife wound on his neck and three wounds on his chest. The scene was very tragic. He immediately reported to the China Bank authorities and then reported to the Public Security Bureau to investigate and arrest the murderer in order to solve the case.

Silver and Money Industries: Striving to Support Industry and Commerce 110

Many Loan Extensions to Securely Get Through the End of the Fourth Month: Factory Representatives Visit Kong Today to Request Loans, according to Xinxin News Agency. Various domestic goods factories and firms in the city are suffering from the effects of monetary tightening, dumping of foreign goods, and the decline of the rural economy, resulting in a sharp reduction in purchasing power, which has led to sluggish business, stockpiling of inventory, and difficulties in capital circulation. Therefore, smaller factories and firms are in a precarious situation. At the same time, the four-month settlement period for long-term loans in the money industry has arrived. They are all striving to find ways to cope with the difficulties. Fortunately, major banks are providing mortgage loans, and money shops are expanding credit loans as much as possible, and are striving to provide assistance and relief. The term of various loans at the end of the fourth month, on average, 70 to 80 percent were extended or repaid in installments. Therefore, there is no problem with the difficulty at the end of the fourth month. However, in order to develop production, most domestic goods factories have sent representatives from the Domestic Goods Promotion Alliance, led by Gu Yuan, to visit President Kong at the Central Bank at 11:00 AM today to request loans for relief from the current difficulties and to develop production. The amount of relief needed by each factory has been filled in separately and submitted to the representative for President Kong to review and approve.

Provisional Measures Agreed Upon Before the Sino-French Vietnam Trade Treaty is Signed: Overseas Chinese Negotiate with Customs Authorities 111

According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, the Sino-French Vietnam Trade Treaty had already been in the process of being drafted during Wang Zhengting's tenure as Foreign Minister. The main treaty had been agreed upon at that time, with only a minor issue on the supplementary treaty causing delays until now, preventing its implementation. When French Minister Mr. Chapon-Baissac returned to China to resume his post, it was once widely rumored that the treaty could be actively concluded. However, there has been no news of any new progress in diplomatic negotiations to date. The Xin Sheng News Agency reporter learned from overseas Chinese affairs circles yesterday that overseas Chinese in Vietnam are subject to various restrictions in their commercial activities due to the lack of treaty protection. For example, the import duty levied by the Vietnamese customs on the same type of Chinese goods can vary arbitrarily from one dollar today to ten dollars tomorrow, with no set standards. This deters many overseas Chinese merchants from engaging in the trade of domestic goods, which has a significant impact on the export of Chinese products. In contrast, goods from other countries that have trade agreements with Vietnam, especially Japanese goods, are continuously imported into Vietnam, threatening the survival of Chinese businesses. Therefore, leading overseas Chinese figures such as Yan Zijun and Chen Liju recently negotiated with the Vietnamese customs authorities in their private capacities and agreed upon a provisional solution to be implemented before the official signing and implementation of the Sino-French Vietnam Trade Treaty. The solution involves the overseas Chinese Chamber of Commerce submitting a list of commonly traded Chinese goods, and the Vietnamese customs will then specify the applicable tax rates for each item on the list and notify the overseas Chinese. However, this is a temporary arrangement, and the customs authorities reserve the right to change the tax rates at any time, provided that the overseas Chinese Chamber of Commerce is notified one week before the change, who will then inform the respective overseas Chinese merchants. It is reported that this provisional measure is now in effect.

Overseas Chinese Federation: Measures to Boycott Siamese Rice 112

Yesterday, it was resolved to take unified action by contacting major ports. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce is requested to convene a meeting on a specific date. According to the Shiye News Agency, the harsh regulations on overseas Chinese education and the restrictions on overseas Chinese industrial and commercial activities promulgated by Siam have aroused deep resentment among the Chinese people. Outraged by this injustice, the Shanghai Overseas Chinese Federation, in addition to making every effort to assist the three million overseas Chinese in Siam, convened an emergency meeting of the fifth organizing committee at its headquarters at 3:30 PM yesterday to discuss ways to unite relevant organizations across the country and plan a large-scale boycott of Siamese rice imports. The committee members present included Guo Shun, Wu Yingpei, Wu Jishun, Xie Denan, and Huang Jianzhong. Guo Shun chaired the meeting, and Chen Luqin recorded the proceedings. After the chairman reported the purpose of the meeting, the committee members expressed their opinions and discussed the proposals. (1) How to deal with the Siamese authorities' oppression of overseas Chinese? It was resolved to strongly support them. (2) Should there be unified communication with relevant organizations in other ports to implement the boycott of Siamese rice? It was resolved to send letters to the chambers of commerce and rice merchants' associations in the major ports where Siamese rice is sold in China, such as Guangzhou, Xiamen, Hong Kong, Shantou, and Shanghai, to seek unified action. (3) How to seek support from relevant organizations in this city for the boycott of Siamese rice? It was resolved to request the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Rice Merchants' Association, and other trade associations to hold a formal meeting on a specific date to discuss assistance measures. (4) Boycotting Siamese rice is a major undertaking, and effective measures should be discussed to achieve significant results. It was resolved that each committee member would be responsible for careful research. The meeting adjourned around 6:00 PM.

Tibet: Awang Nangye Khenpo Comes to Shanghai to Visit Putuo and Lingyin Temples 120

Awang Nangye Khenpo from Tibet, Lhasa, practiced diligently from a young age and became proficient in the scriptures when he grew up. His scholarship and Taoism have always been respected by Tibetans. Later, he was selected by the Dalai Lama as the Geshe of the Serxu Temple in Tibet. Geshe is the Tibetan term for scholar. In the 21st year of the Republic of China (1932), he was ordered by the Dalai Lama to be appointed as the Khenpo of the Guangfa Temple in Maogong, Sichuan, to preach, explain the scriptures, and evangelize the local people. He established himself in Sichuan for three years. The generals in Sichuan who respected him most were Liu Wenhui and Xiang Yuren. During the conflict between the Han and Tibetan peoples in Jinsha River the year before last, Khenpo, based on the principle of compassion, strongly advocated peace and sent Luo Jiaming and others to Changdu and other places to mediate, which finally achieved a satisfactory result. This spring, Khenpo vowed to go south to visit Putuo and Lingyin Temples and tour Beijing and Shanghai along the way. Currently, Khenpo is being kept in Shanghai by his friends for a short stay and resides in Jing'an Villa. He is scheduled to return to Sichuan by ship in early next month.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Telegrams Ministry of Transportation Requesting Cancellation of Simple Postal Package Fees 122

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Ministry of Transportation in Nanjing: "To the Ministry of Transportation, Nanjing. It has been reported by the Jiangxi Ganxian Chinese Medicine Trade Association, Clothing Trade Association, Foreign Goods Trade Association, Dyeing Trade Association, and National Cloth Trade Association that the Gan County Post Office charges an additional simple fee for packages transferred from Ji'an and half an additional simple fee for packages transferred from Guangdong Nanxiong. Now that the highway is completed, transportation is convenient, and automobile transportation fees are decreasing rather than increasing, we have previously requested that you order the cancellation of the fees. We previously received Jiangxi Postal Administration No. 380 for registered mail, acknowledging receipt of the report. We have investigated and found that the Gan County Post Office charges an additional simple fee for packages going to and from various places transferred from Ji'an and half a simple fee for packages transferred from Guangdong Nanxiong because automobile transportation costs are high and they have to appropriately increase fees to make up for it. The proximity of Ji'an and Linchuan to places with railways and waterways varies, so they cannot be compared. Furthermore, the claim in the report that packages from Guangdong Province transferred through Nanxiong are not subject to fees is not true. We received this and investigated. In the past, due to the communist bandits' harassment and the blockade of the Gan River, packages from various places to Gan were transferred from Ji'an by rickshaw. Under these special circumstances, transportation costs increased, and the bureau charged the recipients an additional simple fee to handle the matter, which was not unreasonable. However, when transportation costs returned to normal, the additional fees should be cancelled, as the Postal Administration had previously approved. Now that the communist bandits have fled far away, sailing has returned to normal, and highway transportation is convenient, transportation costs are decreasing rather than increasing, which goes without saying. However, the Postal Administration and the Jiangxi Postal Administration did not order the Gan County Post Office to cancel the increased additional simple fee, but still allow them to charge an additional simple fee for packages transferred from Ji'an and half a simple fee for packages transferred from Nanxiong, claiming that automobile transportation costs are high and they have to appropriately increase fees to make up for it. If automobile transportation costs are high, the Postal Administration should calculate and collect fees from the sender once for all automobile-accessible counties, which would be reasonable. Now, highways have been successively completed throughout Jiangxi Province, and dozens of counties are accessible by automobile. No local post office has been heard of charging recipients additional simple fees, except for the Gan County Post Office, which is allowed to charge an additional simple fee for packages delivered to various places. Taking the Ji-Gan Road as an example, the Wan'an Suichuan Post Office does not need to charge additional simple fees for packages, even though Suichuan and Wan'an are only a little over a hundred li from Gan and are not accessible by railway. Within this hundred li distance, a simple fee must be added. In the same province and both using automobile transportation, the fees are so different, what could be more unfair? It can be seen that the reason for charging additional fees to make up for high automobile transportation costs is completely unfounded. Furthermore, the communist bandits have fled far away, and the Gan River is unobstructed. Sailboats and steamships come and go like shuttles, and transportation has returned to normal. Packages delivered from various places to Gan are sometimes transported by automobile, but most of them are transported by sailboats and steamships to Gan. However, the Gan Post Office still charges a uniform simple fee, which is close to extortion. Therefore, we hereby submit a written request for your examination and approval, and for your forwarding to the National Government, the Ministry of Transportation, and the Nanjing Postal Administration and the Jiangxi Postal Administration, ordering the Gan County Post Office to quickly cancel this additional simple fee to alleviate the difficulties of businesses and facilitate commerce. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce," etc. The matter was previously submitted by the Gan County Chamber of Commerce in December of last year, also by telegram, requesting your approval. No reply has been received yet. The reason for the additional simple fee for postal delivery in that area was due to the obstacles and difficulties in transportation caused by the chaos of the bandits. Therefore, when the bandit chaos is quelled and transportation is restored to normal, the simple fee should be exempted. This is a definite principle. Now, the post office in that area has suddenly changed its tune after the bandit chaos has been quelled, attributing it to the high cost of automobiles. If what they say is true, then the simple fee will become a permanent practice. If this is extrapolated, highways will gradually become widespread throughout the country, but why do they not all charge additional simple fees? This is sufficient to show that the reason given by the bureau is not well-founded. The construction of highways, in addition to facilitating military transportation, was originally intended to facilitate commercial transportation. If the bureau does what it does, the commercial highways will become an excuse to harm businesses, making it impossible to reduce transportation costs and make progress. The ministry should consider the overall situation and correct it. It is reasonable to telegram your bureau for examination and approval, and to order the bureau to cancel all additional simple fees, which would be fair and convenient. The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce respectfully submits this."

And the proposal of Song Shixiang, Jiao Dingen, Shi Qinghua and other ten members to request the association to organize a maintenance association for released prisoners, was not discussed at all. It was decided that the joint meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees would set another date for the general meeting to re-elect officials. At 4:30 PM, the meeting was adjourned.

May your spirit be present, may you accept our offering. Alas, enjoy!

Hai Zhou Merchant Ship Sinks Xin Yu Long Fishing Boat; Ningbo Association Sends Letter to Maritime Bureau Requesting Legal Action 130

Shi Abao from Dinghai makes a living from fresh fish and owns a fresh fish boat named Xin Yu Long, employing ten crew members. On the 21st of this month, the fresh fish boat was hit by ice at Gao Qiao and sailed to the sea off Yushan to collect fresh fish. At 5:00 AM the next morning, as it approached the sea off Tongsha, a light fog filled the air. As dawn was approaching, the crew of the boat vaguely saw a giant wheel in the fog, not sounding its whistle, but sailing quickly towards them. The boat hurriedly steered to avoid it, but the giant wheel also steered in the direction the boat was trying to avoid, colliding with the hull, instantly cutting it in two. All ten crew members fell into the water and called for help. Although the people escaped, the boat sank and the losses were immeasurable. It was later learned that the giant wheel was the Haizhou merchant ship of the Hezhong Company. They attempted to negotiate to shirk responsibility. Yesterday, the boat owner Shi Abao sent a letter to the Ningbo Shanghai Compatriot Association and the Dinghai Shanghai Compatriot Association, requesting assistance. The two associations sent a special letter to the Maritime Bureau based on the situation, which read: "We are writing to inform you that our member Xuan Abao stated that he is engaged in fresh fish trade and owns a boat named Xin Yu Long. On the afternoon of the 22nd of this month, the boat was hit by ice at Gao Qiao and sailed to the sea off Yushan to collect fresh fish. The next morning (the 22nd), as it approached the sea off Tongsha, a light fog suddenly appeared. The driver instructed the crew to be extra careful. Unexpectedly, at 5:25 AM, as dawn was approaching, a giant wheel was vaguely seen in the fog sailing straight towards the boat. The boat, fearing an accident, and with a southeast wind, quickly steered to avoid it. Unexpectedly, the wheel did not follow a straight line but instead steered in the direction the boat was trying to avoid. The ten crew members shouted loudly, but the wheel was traveling fast and could not avoid it, causing the boat to be brutally hit by the wheel's bow at the mast. The force of the impact broke the hull in two, and it was immediately drawn into the wheel's bottom. All ten crew members cried for help. The wheel then realized its negligence and immediately rescued them. However, apart from two people who were rescued safely, the other eight were lost at sea. Their fate is unknown. While investigating, a telegram arrived from Dinghai on the 24th, stating that they had all been rescued. Although the crew members were celebrating their survival, Yu Yuanju purchased the boat for their livelihood. The sudden accident is no less than destroying the entire family's life. The estimated loss includes the boat price of 3,200 yuan, the equipment cost of 2,200 yuan, ice money of 70 yuan, and each of the ten crew members' luggage and clothing worth about 20 yuan, totaling 200 yuan, for a total loss of 5,670 yuan. After the accident, the Maritime Bureau was reported to investigate. The wheel was traveling in heavy fog without sounding its horn and at high speed, which is a violation of navigation regulations. The wheel is the Haizhou merchant ship of the Hezhong Company. The above facts are all true. The wheel should be fully responsible. However, the member is doing business in a foreign land and is weak and easily bullied. The wheel is cunningly shirking responsibility, causing the member's capital and the crew members' clothing to be suddenly destroyed and without compensation. We have always admired your association for helping the weak and suppressing the strong, and for upholding justice. The member has suffered this catastrophe, and his life and family are in danger. Therefore, we are urgently pleading for your assistance in negotiating reasonably and ordering the wheel to pay compensation according to the law to maintain their livelihood. The Haizhou merchant ship did not sound its horn and was traveling at high speed in the heavy fog, which is negligent. Moreover, the fishing boat steered to avoid it, but the wheel did not follow a straight line and collided with the hull, cutting it in two. According to reason and logic, it is difficult to shirk responsibility. Based on the above situation, we hereby jointly request your bureau to preside over the matter and order the Hezhong Company to compensate for the losses to show fairness. We respectfully request your approval for handling and a reply. Sincerely, to the Shanghai Maritime Bureau of the Ministry of Communications. Ningbo Shanghai Compatriot Association Chairman Chu Hede, Dinghai Shanghai Compatriot Association Chairman Liu Hongsheng."

Pudong Cleaning Campaign 131

The Pudong cleaning campaign, which ran from April 25th to 28th, has concluded. One of the unprecedented initiatives in recent decades is noteworthy: the promotion of personal hygiene and improvement of drinking water from local 老虎灶(lao hu zao, old stove teahouses) on the 27th. Bathhouses offered reduced prices, with large pools costing ten coppers and individual tubs half price, drawing large crowds of bathers. At 1:30 PM that afternoon, a meeting was held with all 老虎灶(lao hu zao, old stove teahouses) owners to discuss improving drinking water. Zhang Mingqin, the director of the Pudong branch bureau, gave a speech, stating, "The deadly weapons in the world, such as guns, bombs, and drugs like heroin and red pills, are all tangible and can be prevented. However, intangible bacteria lurking in raw water are even more deadly. Pudong does not have tap water, and the water drawn from the Huangpu River is even more unclean and contains more bacteria. Therefore, in order to protect the lives and safety of the public, you 老虎灶(lao hu zao, old stove teahouses) owners must improve your water by installing sand filtration systems. We will have Mr. Zhang Qinggen, a cadre from the Youth Association, explain the methods to you." Afterwards, Mr. Zhang provided guidance, stating that the materials needed for the equipment include sand, stone, and palm fibers, costing about two yuan each. After listening to the lecture, the 老虎灶(lao hu zao, old stove teahouses) owners were deeply moved and willing to make improvements. At the end, a photo was taken, and the meeting adjourned. The item for the 28th was to clean up the streets of Pudong, with the goal of removing garbage. About 600 people participated in the work, including the 5th branch of the Shanghai Youth Service Corps, the Xiang Sheng Elementary School Boy Scouts, the military band, the Jing Cun Elementary School, the Fu Xin Elementary School, the Pei Dong Public Security Bureau, and the Yang Jing Security Corps, led by General Commander Xu Baoming. The garbage truck team was led by Health Police Chief Yu Yue. After gathering at the Youth Association stadium for a photo, the Xiang Sheng Elementary School Boy Scouts led the way with military music, parading and touring before carrying out the garbage transport work. The stinking ditch on Jingju Road was buried with water pipes and filled with garbage in order to build a road.
