St. Francis Takes the Lead 2-1 in the First Half; Starlight Reverses the Defeat to Win 6-3

Starlight and St. Francis of the Western League's E Group had equal scores, so they played a final at Shenyuan Stadium yesterday morning at 10:00 AM to determine who would win the championship. The situation was very plain, but both sides' offense and defense were very balanced. In the first half, St. Francis took a 2-1 lead. In the second half, Starlight gave it their all, and their luck turned, scoring five goals one after another. In the end, Starlight reversed the defeat to win 6-3.

First Half: Starlight kicked off and attacked first, but was intercepted halfway. St. Francis took the opportunity to attack, coming fiercely. In addition, Starlight faced the wind, so they were under pressure. The ball was constantly hovering in front of the Starlight goal. After ten minutes, St. Francis' Corassa got the ball and crossed it, and Koumani ran up and kicked the ball into the upper right corner. Not long after, Starlight's Liu Shiqing detoured and infiltrated, breaking through the enemy's goal, creating a 1-1 situation. Afterwards, the offense and defense of both sides were quite fierce, and they were deadlocked for a long time. The St. Francis center forward attacked the goal, and the Starlight goalkeeper slapped the ball out, but Koumani added another kick, and it was impossible to save. At the end of the first half, St. Francis took a 2-1 lead.

Second Half: Starlight gave it their all and tried to cheer up. Xue Yongyuan dribbled the ball deep and shot from 12 yards away, flying into the upper right corner of the goal, creating a 2-2 tie again. Once, Xue Yongyuan dribbled the ball close to the enemy's goal, and St. Francis' inner defender Raig hurriedly resisted, but accidentally pushed the ball into his own net. From then on, Starlight's luck came. Lin Qingchi headed and kicked, and Xue Yongyuan shot from a distance, killing the barbarian army and leaving them with no way out. At the end of the game, St. Francis got a penalty kick opportunity and pulled back a goal. In the end, Starlight reversed the defeat to win 6-3.

Economic Supplement

New Ways to Develop Export Trade (Continued) 194

— Kong Dian

Speaking further from the perspective of trade finance, the urgent need is equally felt. The rise and fall of foreign exchange business invariably shifts with the development of the trade industry. The main source of profit for exchange banks lies in discounting import and export bills. Therefore, the close relationship between the two is like that of lips and teeth. It is inconceivable that banks engaged in foreign exchange can maintain profits on their own when trade shrinks. Consequently, traders rely on foreign exchange banks for the movement of funds for their import and export goods, which is enough to control their business life. The credit risks associated with export trade also have a significant impact on the exchange banks themselves. If these risks can somehow be managed so that foreign exchange banks do not bear part of the responsibility, they will naturally dare to take bold steps and provide exporters with financing facilities in a simple and convenient manner.

The settlement of payments in import and export trade is mostly done through documentary bills. When foreign exchange banks purchase documentary bills, they usually use documentary letters of credit to prevent any unforeseen risks. Because the issuing bank of the letter of credit assumes the guarantee responsibility, they are happy to purchase them, handing over the amount specified on the bill to the holder. Otherwise, who would be willing to inquire? However, since the issuing bank assumes this guarantee responsibility, it will inevitably charge the importer, who is the client, a certain issuing fee or other acceptance fee as special compensation. In this way, the importer will feel that the burden is too heavy and will not dare to import goods rashly, which will create obstacles to export trade.

To eliminate the above-mentioned obstacles and allow a country's export trade to proceed smoothly, the only way is to implement export credit insurance. However, in terms of technology, measuring risks in this system is very difficult. If it is run by private individuals, it is feared that their financial resources will be insufficient. Therefore, most countries today take on this responsibility through the government. The following is a brief description of the experiences of countries such as England and Germany in handling this matter.

II

The export credit insurance system originated in England. In 1919, the British Board of Trade studied the reasons for the decline in trade with Central Europe and concluded that it was due to the financial difficulties of exporters. Therefore, on September 20 of that year, the Overseas Trade Act was promulgated, with the Treasury allocating £25 million, up to 80% of the value of the goods, specifically for lending to merchants engaged in export trade. Although this law provided exporters with temporary financing convenience, it still lacked guarantees for export bills and insurance for credit risks. Therefore, after consultation with the Federation of National Chambers of Commerce, the law was revised, and the Overseas Trade Credit Insurance Amendment Act was promulgated in June 1921. A special department was set up within the Board of Trade to manage it. For export bills issued by exporters when selling goods to overseas merchants, with a term of less than one year, the government would guarantee the full amount of the bill. For terms exceeding one year, the limit was 85%. At the same time, it was stipulated that the government retained the right of recourse for 57.5% from the exporter in the former case and 42.5% in the latter. The scope of application was initially limited to countries in Central and Southern Europe, but later expanded to India, Ceylon, and the Far East. By 1925, all goods exported overseas, except to Soviet Russia, could be insured. At the same time, the government convened a committee in July 1925, composed of national industrialists, bankers, and insurance officials, to discuss (1) the benefits of export credit insurance for export trade; (2) whether the government needs to take other measures to supplement existing benefits; and (3) if necessary, what specific methods should be adopted. After research, the committee submitted the following opinions in March of the following year:

(1) Credit insurance is essential for healthy export trade.

(2) The current system still cannot meet the demands of exporters.

(3) The government should find ways to expand the current system without causing excessive trading.

Therefore, the government was recommended to formulate three measures, namely:

A. For bills issued by exporters, if they are of the Without Recourse type (i.e., the drawer has no right of recourse), the government will provide a guarantee of up to 75% of the face value. In other words, if the overseas importer who is responsible for payment refuses to pay in the future, the bank that discounted the bill can request repayment of the guaranteed amount and seek it from the exporter by other means.

B. Conversely, for bills issued by exporters, if they are of the (With full recourse) type (i.e., the drawer is obliged to repay the face value), the government will guarantee the full amount of the face value. At first glance, exporters seem to have no insurance benefits at all because they are obliged to repay the full amount of the bill. However, after the bill is guaranteed by the government, it can be discounted by the bank without having to provide additional collateral, which is indeed very convenient.

C. With reference to the above two, for bills issued by exporters, either (Without recourse) or after consultation with the insurance authorities regarding the extent of their repayment obligation, the government will guarantee all or part of the face value as they wish.

The government implemented this proposal in July 1926, and in 1927, it expanded the business of the insurance department, allowing exporters to agree with the insurance department to target all their importing partners and establish a comprehensive insurance contract, setting a guarantee limit. When issuing documentary bills, they would notify the insurance department to guarantee them within the set limit. If the exporter does not issue bills or the amount of bills issued is very small, the government may refund part of the insurance premium already paid.

The most common contracts between exporters and the government now are two types: one is that after the exporter pays the insurance premium, if the documentary bills issued are rejected by importers in other countries, the government will compensate 75% of the face value; the other is to provide the exporter's bank with an unconditional payment guarantee for a certain amount, which is particularly convenient for exporters to obtain financing. The guarantee period varies depending on the type of goods, with a maximum of five years for machinery and a minimum of only six months for piece goods. This system has been in operation for over fifteen years. It was originally scheduled to end at the end of 1935, but in the current environment where the world economy has not yet escaped the panic, there is no doubt that this effective method of revitalizing trade will continue to be implemented.

IV

Following England, Germany was the next to use export credit insurance as a strategy to revitalize overseas trade. Private insurance companies in Germany, such as Hermes Kreditversicherungsbank and Frankfurter Allgeneine Versicherungsgesellschaft, used to insure the risks of export bills, but the high fees made it ineffective. Therefore, in 1922, the government began to cooperate with Hermes, first with a fund of 30 million marks, to launch long-term export credit insurance to Russia in 1922. Subsequently, it was gradually increased, and by 1927, it was extended to other countries. The method is that when the exporter ships the goods to the foreign buyer, they can use the bill of lading as evidence and apply for insurance to the insurance company. The insurance company, after retaining a portion, can reinsure half of its insured amount with the Export Kredit-Versicherung-Stelle established by the government, with the state as the reinsurer. If the price of the goods cannot be recovered in the future and the loss is too large, the excess will be fully compensated by the government. Therefore, not only do exporters have this guarantee to sign export credit insurance contracts as their only defensive weapon, but insurance companies also do not hesitate regardless of which merchant the goods are sold to or the excessive amount of insurance. Moreover, after insuring, if the exporter mortgages the insurance policy to the bank, the insurance company can certify that it will pay the compensation to the bank holding the policy in the event of a loss. In this way, in one transfer, the exporter's turnover of export funds is not only not subject to the government's previous loans, but they can also collect the goods with ease.

In addition to England and Germany, Sweden, Norway, Italy, and Austria have also followed suit. In May 1930, Japan enacted this type of insurance under the name of the Export Compensation Law, stipulating that for domestic goods exported to designated areas overseas, if the bank purchases the issued documentary bills and suffers losses due to non-performance of the insurance, the bank will pay a certain compensation fee, and the government will compensate 70% of its losses. It has been implemented for over five years, and its export trade has been expanding day by day. Although there are many reasons for this, export credit insurance is undoubtedly an important factor in promoting this trend.

Looking back at our country, to this day, the domestic economic situation is gradually becoming depleted due to the continuous increase in annual import surpluses and the outflow of cash. In the future, to prevent economic collapse and balance international payments, the development of overseas trade should be taken as the only prerequisite. The government should first follow the established examples of various countries and implement export credit insurance, so that merchants engaged in export can rest assured that their goods are shipped and sold abroad, and provide buyers with long-term credit facilities. In this way, foreign importers will naturally be happy to purchase our country's products. By doing this, the quantity of imported goods will be more than offset by the increase in exports, so why worry about the imbalance of international borrowing? However, today in our country, there are only one or two overseas exchange banks, and they have all been established recently. They lack sufficient experience in investigating overseas market conditions, and there are few who are directly engaged in export trade. Not to mention that in this time of financial constraints, the government is powerless to do so, and even if it spends huge sums of money and takes risks, the effect is still questionable. In our humble opinion, since the world economy is still groaning under the tide of panic, it is practically impossible for our country to increase exports for a while. For the present, it is better to first abolish various obstacles in domestic trade, such as transit taxes and part of the business tax, as soon as possible, so that domestic products can reduce costs and circulate freely. Then unnecessary foreign goods will naturally be ignored. With our country's natural advantages, why worry that it cannot be self-sufficient! (The End)

Two Paths of Today's World Economy 195

— Feng Cihang

Today's world economy is clearly divided into two major groups: those maintaining the gold standard and those having abandoned it. The former group claims that the revival of the world economy lies in the resumption of the gold standard by the latter group. The latter group argues that the recovery of global prosperity requires the gold standard group to temporarily abandon it as well, and collectively work towards raising world prices. These two major groups have engaged in heated debates over these two opposing paths, even at the previous World Economic Conference, and it remains the biggest problem in the world. In theory, which of these two paths is the correct one? Many world economists are constantly discussing it. In reality, which path is the world's economy heading towards today? People all over the world are watching intently. A Washington dispatch on April 21st reported that the United States is preparing to convene another World Economic Conference within the next six months to discuss this issue.

Our country is currently experiencing an economic panic, with the situation becoming increasingly serious. However, our economic panic is not something we created ourselves; it is indeed a product of the global economic panic. Although the United States' silver purchase policy is sufficient to fuel our economic panic and accelerate its realization, the occurrence of our economic panic is not entirely the result of the U.S. silver purchase. If the United States did not purchase silver, would we encounter the same difficulties? I think the timing might be sooner or later, but the calamity of the panic would probably be difficult to avoid! Because currency devaluation competition among countries would also gradually raise the external price of our silver currency, leading to the same result of monetary contraction. Therefore, we are now, like the gold standard countries, also wavering on the diverging roads of two paths. One is to adhere to our silver standard, patiently hoping and waiting for the arrival of global prosperity, or a change in the U.S. silver purchase policy. The other is to ban silver exports, suspend cash payments, inflate the currency, break away from the shackles of the world economy, and let the price of the national currency plummet.

However, whether in China or the world, both of the aforementioned possible paths are fraught with thorns and danger, so neither is a good option. Therefore, everyone is hesitating and wavering, wandering on the diverging roads, unable to move forward or retreat, forming a stalemate of shifting from left to right. Now let us put aside theory and observe the actual effects of the economic policies adopted by major countries under this panic situation based on actual statistical figures. The facts tell us that countries that have lowered their currency prices have made relatively significant progress in saving the panic and restoring the market. For example, if we study the characteristics of world trade in 1934, the trade of countries with currency devaluation, such as the United States, Britain, and Japan, has indeed significantly recovered, while the trade of countries maintaining the gold standard, such as France and Germany, has been shrinking day by day and still tending towards decline. Although various measures hindering the progress of world trade, such as exchange controls, tariff increases, import restrictions, and import bans, were prevalent in various countries last year, the trade of countries with lower exchange rates, especially Britain and the United States, has gradually recovered to the state of 1931; Japan's progress is particularly rapid, having broken the trade figures of 1928 and 1929. On the other hand, among the European countries, such as France, exports and imports are only tending to decline; although Germany has been striving to improve the trade balance, the result is still a decline in exports and an increase in imports, with the years of trade surplus having transformed into a trade deficit.

Britain's imports last year were £732.2 million, an increase of £57 million compared to 1933. Exports were £447 million, an increase of £30 million. The import surplus was £285.2 million, an increase of £27 million compared to 1933, but a decrease of over £100 million compared to 1932. That is, under the condition of increased import and export trade, the import surplus has been reduced, indicating that its domestic economic situation has improved. Last year, the United States had imports of $1.6555 billion and exports of $2.134 billion, an increase of $100.5 million in imports and $459 million in exports compared to 1933. The export surplus was $479 million, more than double the increase compared to 1933 ($215 million in 1933), the highest record since 1930. Last year, Japan had imports of 2.313 billion yuan, an increase of 363 million yuan. Exports were 2.2 billion yuan, an increase of 330 million yuan. The import surplus was 123 million yuan, an increase of 44.4 million yuan compared to 1933.

Although the state of trade progress in the above three countries, Britain, the United States, and Japan, each has its special conditions, such as the extraordinary increase in trade between Britain and Canada, South Africa, Australia, India, and the three Scandinavian countries as a result of the Ottawa Conference, as well as the United States' efforts in the development of the South American market and Japan's focus on the invasion of the Manchurian market, these are also reasons for their trade growth, the devaluation of currency in each country is indeed a common and major reason. Because in politics, although there are relationships of territories and colonies, in economics, it is necessary to look at the actual commercial conditions. For example, if a country's currency is of high value, then the people of the territory and colony will inevitably switch directions to purchase cheaper foreign goods, and they cannot simply use political power to force the people of the territory and colony to love and use domestic goods. Because this kind of coercion is ineffective.

June and July of 1932 were the worst times for the world economy. At that time, industrial productivity fell by 30% compared to 1929, prices plummeted, unemployment increased, the countryside declined, and the phenomenon of economic panic permeated the globe. Government authorities and economists in various countries were racking their brains, anxiously trying to find ways to save the situation. After countless rounds of heated debate, they finally decided to adopt a kind of gradual monetary inflation policy, which was to devalue their own currency in order to open up sales channels for surplus products. After doing this for two or three years, prices gradually increased, unemployment decreased, and all economic conditions tended toward recovery. However, the progress of this recovery was very slow. Especially in the United States, their government spent millions of dollars on revival, but the achievements were very symbolic. What is the reason for this? According to the observation of world-renowned economist Professor Cassel, it is blamed on European countries such as France and Germany for reluctantly maintaining the gold standard, creating a state of domestic contraction. Because the markets of countries maintaining the gold standard still tend to be depressed, which also prevents the markets of countries that have abandoned the gold standard from advancing vigorously and recovering. Therefore, he advocates that gold standard countries such as France and Germany should also temporarily abandon the gold standard, and negotiate with countries such as Britain, the United States, and Japan on the parity of currencies between countries, reduce the fineness of gold coins, and restore the gold standard at the same time. In short, his opinion is that only by reducing the fineness of gold coins in various countries can the world economy be restored.

At present, the world's currency system can be roughly divided into two types: gold-group currency and paper currency-group currency. Although the United States and Germany seem close to the gold group, they are actually not members of the gold group. The gold group strongly advocates restoring the gold standard according to the original statutory parity. The paper money group advocates first restoring the usual relationship between prices and production costs, and then stabilizing the currency's purchasing power over goods. In other words, it advocates raising overall prices first, and then engaging in stabilization. The currency policy of the United Kingdom is representative of the latter. Now many paper money countries' currencies use the pound sterling as the standard, following its rise and fall. British territories and countries such as Sweden, Norway, Denmark, and Argentina are all members of the pound sterling group. The Japanese exchange rate has always followed the pound sterling, and now our country's gold unit is also calculated according to the pound sterling. Secondly, the power of the US dollar group is also very strong. Therefore, according to the current situation, the power of the gold group such as France is very small: it is definitely not as great as the power of the paper currency group. Moreover, according to economic theory, it is easier for a country's currency to depreciate than to appreciate. Now the currencies of various paper group countries have already fallen to 60%, 50%, or 40% of their original value, and the United States has openly reduced the fineness of gold dollars in law, indicating that it has no intention of lifting the ban at the old parity. Therefore, in fact, trying to get the paper group to accommodate the gold group is something that cannot be done. Moreover, the countries in the paper group have now achieved the practical effect of improving trade and restoring the economy by using the method of currency devaluation. Seeing that the gold group countries are all sinking into monetary contraction, falling prices, and depressed industries, they are not willing to quickly restore the gold standard and repeat their mistakes. Moreover, the world's prices have not yet reached the level desired by the paper group countries. They are still actively carrying out various economic revival methods to raise prices. If these are ineffective, or if the effectiveness is very slight, they also seem to not hesitate to sacrifice further and reduce the value of their currency. Therefore, not only do they have no intention of accommodating the gold group, but they also believe that the gold group is the biggest obstacle to the world's economic recovery. The reason why world prices cannot actively rise is because of the gold group's drag. Various efforts of the paper group countries to restore the economy have been discounted in effect and reduced in color due to the existence of the gold group. Therefore, they say that if the world is to quickly return to the road to prosperity, then unless the gold group countries also abandon the gold standard at the same time.

The countries in the gold group were originally France, Italy, Belgium, the Netherlands, Switzerland, Germany, etc., with France as the leader, but now the members of the group have also moved. After the Great War, due to the wasteland of agricultural affairs and the increase in import surplus, the French government issued huge amounts of public debt to revive the war zone. Therefore, the French currency began to plummet wildly from 1919, becoming unbearable. The people suffered the pain of currency inflation. It was not until June 1928 that the gold content of the French franc was reduced by 80% and the gold standard was restored. At that time, some people said that the price of the French franc had fallen too much. However, France's trade developed because of this, and at that time, countries such as Britain and the United States caused a state of contraction. How would they know that after three years, the situation changed, and countries such as Britain and the United States successively abandoned the gold standard in order to avoid the state of contraction, which in turn created a state of contraction for France and other countries. As the currencies of the paper group and other countries depreciated day by day, the currencies of the gold group and other countries appreciated day by day. In other words, the more the paper group's currency depreciated, the more expensive the price of the gold group's currency calculated in the paper group's currency. This expensiveness is not natural, but because the gold group's currency can be exchanged for cash, following the rise and fall of cash. The depreciation of the paper group's currency against cash is the depreciation against the gold group's currency, so the higher the price of gold, the higher the gold group's currency, and the more difficult it is for the gold group to maintain the gold standard. Because everyone thinks that the evaluation of the gold group's currency is too expensive, they will naturally abandon the gold group's currency to exchange cash, silver goods and paper currencies of paper group countries. The factual manifestation of this abandonment is cash payment, squeeze, cash outflow, or hoarding, reducing the reserve of banknotes day by day. If the gold group country cannot cope, it will be forced to abandon the gold standard. Now the gold standard countries are always in this dangerous and uneasy state. The countries in the paper group indirectly accepted major influences. The world's economy is therefore difficult to recover quickly, and trade is therefore difficult to develop rationally.

Indeed, the current evaluation of gold group currency is too great. According to the statistics of September 1934, the percentage of gold group currency to the pound sterling is as follows: that is, the Belgian currency is 7% more expensive than the pound sterling, Italy is 13% more expensive, France is 17% more expensive, the Netherlands is 12% more expensive, Switzerland is 41% more expensive, and Germany is 57% more expensive. This is indeed an extremely unnatural state. If the gold group countries do not take the simultaneous devaluation method, trying to use exchange controls, trade control, and other measures to hinder international trade to prevent the dumping of paper group countries is a counter-current movement, and the result must be failure.

The London Economic Magazine published an article by British economist Mr. Strachey-Galsworthy in January of this year. He also said that to restore world prosperity, countries around the world must simultaneously reduce the fineness of gold coins and restore the gold standard at the same time. According to his statistics, the current gold reserve of various countries is estimated to be £2.272 billion according to the old fineness of 1928. Among them, the gold group countries account for 38%, the United States accounts for 33%, and the remaining countries account for 29%. If the fineness of the currencies of various countries is reduced by an average of 60%, then the world's gold reserve can be increased to £4.863 billion in an instant. The panic of world cash shortage can disappear. As for the implementation steps, he advocated the following: (1) Convene an international economic conference. (2) Increase prices by reducing fineness. (3) Stabilize exchange rates under the agreed equilibrium state of various countries. (4) Increase the contact between the central banks of various countries. (5) Strive to increase the gold reserves of the central banks of various countries. (6) Abolish the exchange controls, import and export restrictions, and other systems that hinder free trade. (7) The solution to the war debt indemnity problem.

The world today is still in the era of the selfish opposition of capitalist countries. The failure of the London Economic Conference can be taken as a lesson. Today's world economy is still living in a confusing and dull age under the confrontation between the gold group and the low group. However, according to the observations of several world-renowned economists, they all say that the road to restoring world prosperity is either for countries to compromise with each other to jointly reduce the fineness of gold coins and restore the gold standard; or for the gold group countries to be unable to endure it and be forced to abandon the gold standard, to raise the general prices in the world, and then restore the gold standard in succession. They all think that in the end, it will not be out of these two paths.

Suggestions for Cooperation Between Shanghai Fish Market and Fish Dealers 196

— Chen Qin Sun

In order to revitalize the fishing industry, the Ministry of Industry established a large-scale fish market in Shanghai, with modern construction and equipment, which is quite perfect. In the future, fresh fish can be preserved and processed to seek a good price; there will be no more corruption that is difficult to last, and it is urgent to sell the goods, which damages the blood. However, the organization of the fish market is entirely state-owned, and merchants are not involved; therefore, it cannot gain the trust of the fish industry, forming a confrontational situation, and it is still difficult to open it. I think that if there is sincerity between the Ministry of Industry and the fish dealers, there is no need for meaningless disputes, but only to firmly adhere to the premise of mutual trust and common trust to seek cooperation. Otherwise, what both sides call benefiting the fishermen will make the fishermen even more confused.

The fish dealers have a tooth permit, which is a legally protected broker. Fishermen venture out to sea to catch fish, relying entirely on fish dealers to lend them capital, which is repaid by selling the catch. However, it is borrowed as it is repaid, eventually accumulating to a huge number. At present, this "fish loan" of Shanghai fish dealers is estimated to be a total of 2.5 million yuan, with an average of about 100,000 yuan per household. After the establishment of the fish market, the fish dealers may lose their original position, so how to handle this fish loan? I hope you will not let the fish dealers suffer the loss alone, which would hinder the progress of the fish market. How about using the original fish dealers as brokers for the fish market? The brokers should be fully responsible for sales, and all accounts of vendors should be handled by the brokers themselves; the fish dealers should transfer all the previous 2.5 million yuan of fish loan claims to the fish market for acceptance. The method of transferring claims can be that the fish market presents to the competent authority to issue a kind of fish industry reorganization and repayment bond. The fund for this bond is designated to be allocated from the fish market's monthly commission income. According to recent statistics, the annual trade volume of Shanghai fish products averages 20 million yuan. The commission is 8% of the value, according to the precedent, and the total annual income is 1.6 million yuan. The fish market and the brokers divide the 8% commission rate, and we assume the ratio is 5 to 3, then the net commission income of the fish market is 1 million yuan per year. If half of it, 500,000 yuan, is allocated to the bond fund, it can be paid off in installments within five years. Or it may be that what the fish dealers get is only a ledger changed to a face value, and the fish dealers are in the position of a broker, and because of the lack of circulating cash, a clever woman cannot cook without rice. Therefore, in addition to the above-mentioned fund for the bond, all of its property (estimated value of more than 1 million yuan) should be provided as a priority collateral, and the Ministry of Industry should be a joint guarantor, stating the bond. If so: the material and spiritual conditions of this bond are complete, and if someone holds it to discuss with the financial sector, the financial sector will surely be happy to cooperate, and all difficulties will be solved easily, and the development of the fishing industry can be predicted.

Securities Last Week, the Northern Faction Dumped the Most Debentures 198

From April 22nd to 27th last week, the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange was in a week of transition between the old and new futures contracts for April and June. At the beginning of the week, prices rose slightly due to a squeeze as the settlement date approached. Towards the weekend, prices fell back due to some rumors. The market generally lacked special fluctuations and remained in a state of consolidation. The bankruptcies of Yongxing and Tongtai money shops occurred when futures contracts were nearing settlement and causing a squeeze, without causing any significant impact. The price of American silver continued to rise without any sign of stopping, deeply affecting the domestic financial market. Interbank lending was barely sufficient to prevent a major collapse, leaving people uneasy and restless. Consequently, many transferred their deposits to foreign banks, and a significant number engaged in arbitrage. The fundamental reason for this is the undeniable financial problem. Future trends will depend on government support. A large amount of the 1996 public bonds are held on account, and any slight easing will lead to short covering. Therefore, even though they are practically worthless, there is still much arbitrage trading, preventing a sharp decline. Last week, the Northern Faction emerged due to the bankruptcies of the two money shops, selling at prices about one-tenth to one-half of a dollar lower. Monday was the last day for April futures, and there was a slight squeeze. Although the money market was tight, the official rate was raised to 43 cents, and market prices rebounded sharply, with short covering pushing prices up by one dollar. Friday was a market holiday for the settlement of April futures. Grains: Hexia Rice Recovers by 10-20 Cents 201

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the supply from various gangs was particularly scarce, with only deliveries from the 16th and 17th (totaling over 3,000 dan). Introduction to the "Insurance Yearbook" 203

The Insurance Yearbook is a creative work and a necessary book for the times. The development of the insurance industry is closely related to the development of industry and commerce, as well as the cultivation of general wealth. Chinese people are generally unfamiliar with the insurance business, which prevents them from using it for prevention and wealth accumulation. This book can fill this gap by providing detailed investigation and records of the business nature of the insurance industry and the current state of the insurance industry both in China and abroad, making it a valuable reference for general use. Edited by Shen Leichun and others from the Chinese Insurance Yearbook Editorial Office, and published by the China Life Insurance Promotion Association.

Free Talk

Linguists Dabbling in Literature 204

— Leng Mo

The study of linguistics generally includes how to write well. And good writing is commonly referred to as literature. Therefore, linguists naturally tend to also become writers. In an environment that worships experts, the position of a linguist may be better than that of a writer. For example, when Liu Bannong was referred to as a writer because he was a linguist, some people complained for him, regretting this. But the general trend is that movie stars are more popular than writers, and writers are more popular than specialized scholars. Is it possible that some linguists, for the sake of popularity, would rather be known as writers? This is worth considering. Although we cannot ask Mr. Bannong in the afterlife, I'm afraid there are others who can give a definite answer.

Liu Xunyu said that many people in Chinese academic fields dabble in literature, but unfortunately, when they do science, it's purely science, and when they do literature, it's purely literature. They have no intention of building a bridge to connect science and literature (paraphrased). Linguists dabbling in literature are the same. But linguistics itself is close to being a bridge between science and literature. Therefore, when linguists dabble in literature, it's purely literature, as if they are deliberately distinguishing between the two. It's difficult to understand why this is the case. Perhaps it is to avoid entering an ivory tower.

Specialized works are generally not very compatible with general reading materials. When treatises on linguistics were very common, *Yu Si* also published articles on the authenticity of the *Zuo Zhuan* and ancient phonology, and *Xin Yue* also published articles on the rigorous study of entering tones. These great works naturally made general readers feel bored. Therefore, after that, there were very few treatises on language published outside of specialized academic journals. Furthermore, the linguistic treatises in specialized publications became increasingly distant from the interests of the general public. In fact, there are many issues related to linguistics that are of great interest to the general public, and it is not impossible to reconcile them with general publications. Going to the smallest details to study specialized knowledge does not seem to be the only pursuit of specialized scholars. Linguists often say this is essential. But if we want to know the pronunciation of a word in a certain dialect, we still have to look for dialect dictionaries compiled by foreigners. There isn't even a Shanghainese dictionary compiled by locals. This seems to be the fault of linguists who are only engaged in lofty or irrelevant pursuits.

Recently, problems that are often touched upon, such as spoken language, handwritten characters, typos, phonetic typefaces, and literacy primers, are all closely related to linguistics. However, there seem to be very few linguists who discuss these problems. Seeing Wang Yile's "Conservatism of Characters" on the issue of typos in *The Independent Critic* made me feel very fortunate. Perhaps this small opinion from a linguistics professor is no less effective than his translations of many famous French literary works. The writer Zhou Zuoren said that he wondered whether it was better to have studied for a long period of time or to have studied in the navy for six years, so he was preparing to "abandon writing for martial arts." Although this is still humorous, it is truly believed that it is inevitable to be a square peg, but one cannot help but hope that linguists would abandon writing for language.

A Sequel to The Travels of Lao Can 205

— Han Feng

Although only six chapters of "A Sequel to The Travels of Lao Can" remain, its content constitutes a complete "Biography of Yi Yun." Mr. Liu Dajun believes that this nun of the Doumu Palace on Mount Tai, who had a great awakening, has lived in his heart for ten years. Mr. Lin Yutang also wrote a preface, believing that "if there really is such a person in the Doumu Palace, I must go to Mount Tai." In Liu Tieyun's writing, Yi Yun is truly worthy of being an extraordinary person who has seen through the cause and effect of the material world. However, when I finished reading this incomplete copy in one go, the impression I got was different from those of the two gentlemen, and my feelings were beyond the character of Yi Yun.

Looking back at the twenty chapters of the original "The Travels of Lao Can," Liu Tieyun liked to entrust his ideals to extraordinary people in the novel. And these extraordinary people must conform to his own ideals: pure, unconstrained, otherworldly, and having a great understanding of human society. Of course, such people cannot be found in the human world. In order to suit his romantic ideals, he had to use his talent to create them. Due to the suitability of various conditions in the ideals of the people of the old era, and the author's own psychological reasons, this created ideal character inevitably fell on a woman. Therefore, in the original book, he created a Yu Gu, and in the sequel, he could not help but create another Yi Yun.

Liu Tieyun was not only unconstrained but also very romantic. Therefore, at any time, he coexisted with the "true self" and the "ideal self." In the original travels, there was Lao Can, and then there was a Yu Gu; in the sequel, he wrote about Lao Can and then created Yi Yun. Lao Can represents a person with a stronger human nature, while Yu Gu and Yi Yun are his surreal ideals, a creation of an idealistic view of life and the world. Reading "The Travels of Lao Can" without focusing on this point makes it very difficult to gain a deep understanding of the author. Only by understanding this point can one understand why Liu Tieyun, who had a scientific mind, added these two fabricated characters to "The Travels of Lao Can," which was very realistic.

Although Yu Gu and Yi Yun are both embodiments of Liu Tieyun's ideals, Yi Yun is more developed in substance. The effort spent on writing Yi Yun was greater than that spent on writing Yu Gu, because this was his more ideal and more sublime shadow, the condensation of his later life view and the creation of the universe. In the talks of Yu Gu, the principles of mutual reference of the three religions are reflected. By his later years, when writing the sequel, he completely placed the focus on Buddhism.

Perhaps because it was ultimately an ideal and could not be cut off from the human world, there were still many complaints and dissatisfactions with the existing world. From Yi Yun's conversations, one can see how rampant the officials were at that time and understand how ugly the human world was. Without decisively separating from the human world, readers feel related to this character, and the success of this character's creation lies in this, and the author's success also lies in this. As for Yi Yun's self-description of the process of jumping out of the emotional bonds, this is completely the compassionate heart of Lao Can, who uses a rattle to transcend the human world, telling the reader how to transcend the ordinary and enter the sacred. This is why Lao Can sent Cui Huan into the temple without hesitation. In his later years, Liu Tieyun, after suffering various setbacks, although his passion remained, he inevitably had a sense of fatigue.

To understand Liu Tieyun's later thoughts, and for those who have read the original book, this sequel to "The Travels of Lao Can" is worth reading. But I don't agree with what Liu Dajun said, that the writing style is superior to the original book. Writing about Yi Yun's psychology is indeed a new realm in Liu Tieyun's creation, but many of the excellent parts of the original book, such as Daming Lake, Wang Xiaoyu, and the Yellow River water fetching scenes, are not inferior to the success of dissecting Yi Yun's psychology. Saying that there is new development in the description, I completely agree. Furthermore, the main reason for the success of the original book lies in the realism of social life and his relatively scientific method. Although there is the ideal Yu Gu, the focus is not on this aspect, and the impression that readers can get is a sense of reality. The sequel is the opposite, because it only wrote about Yi Yun, the realistic component is lighter. Although it feels pleasing when reading, it ultimately feels like reading an "ideal novel." The whole book is just a beginning, of course, it cannot be used to make a conclusion. However, there is no need to give the sequel a higher rating than the original book in any aspect.

On the Asahan River 206

— Fei Er

The Asahan River, once a disputed territory between the Chinese and Malays, is the seat of the governor who rules over us Orientals—Orientals, except for Japan, implying those who are ruled. For two years, I had repeatedly thought of going there, but I could never make it happen due to various reasons. This time, I finally made the trip.

In the morning, as the Singapore-Raja steamer turned from the open sea into the Asahan River, the river's current grandly welcomed us, and the achievements of the Chinese fishermen were displayed before our eyes.

At the mouth of the Asahan River, starting from the first row of fish-trapping structures erected by Chinese fishermen deep into the sea, the steamer passed through the fishermen's pillar-stakes for several hours. The Chinese, with their strong and hardworking bodies tanned by the scorching sun, raised sails and cast nets on the Asahan River. Looking out from the steamer, one could see fishermen everywhere on the river, carrying their catches and combating the tropical sun with healthy laughter. Because I had been in K City and had mingled with these fishermen, I knew a little about their way of life; so when I saw the joy they enjoyed after working and harvesting, laughter also welled up deeply in my own heart.

I silently blessed the people who catch fish and shrimp, saying, "The seas of the Pacific and Indian Oceans are yours, and so are the seas of the vast Nanyang Archipelago."

Watching the fishermen with their bare, dark bodies, using their strong arms to pull up the net ropes from the sea and river, or even diving deep into the water to fight fierce fish, yet calmly surfacing with a triumphant smile, I shared in their joy. Or when the tide rose, and waves constantly crashed against their small fishing boats, but our fishermen bravely continued their work, letting their small boats float and sink in the waves, a sense of admiration and envy welled up in my heart:

"What am I, compared to them? Look at the sons of the earth, these masters of the sea!" Thinking of their rugged life journey, I felt an unusual sense of shame.

Due to the current, the boat often sailed close to the shore, sometimes hugging the left bank and sometimes the right. As the boat moved at a sluggish pace, within a foot or so of the shore, the river water, buffeted by the ship, constantly splashed waves onto the beach, creating a splashing sound. Near the riverbank, coconut groves were constantly being eroded, and occasionally one or two coconut trees would fall sideways into the river, their treetops leaning precariously into the water. On the shore, monkeys were often seen playing in the wild vines, coconut groves, or attap thickets. As soon as the steamer approached, the passengers would make "hissing" sounds at them, and the young monkeys would hide in their mothers' arms.

On the white foam churned up by the river, various tree trunks and pieces of wood rushed along with the rapid current; boats sped by like arrows; or there were boatmen wearing Turkish-style hats, using hand-operated oars, and covered with attap leaf canopies, ready to carry passengers, but their postures were unusually lazy.

Along the riverbanks, houses covered with attap leaves were often found, sparsely half-hidden among the coconut groves. A ladder hung from the bank into the river; Malay women held their children and stood at the end of the ladder, staring at the steamer.

Once the boat reached Bagan, the port of Asahan, the travelers' hearts were filled with joy. Bagan is a port city where fishermen gather, displaying a splash of red amidst the greenery, with the messy corners of attap houses facing the travelers. As the boat approached, the streets along the shore were clearly visible. Fishermen walked along the streets in twos and threes, or stopped to gaze at the steamer.

As soon as the boat stopped in the river, Chinese coolies rowed wooden boats loaded with fishing products close to the ship. The stench of salted fish and shrimp pierced the nostrils of the passengers from the piles of cargo. The sound of machinery suddenly became noisy, and cranes loaded package after package of goods into the ship's hold. Afterward, the Dutch captain frowned on the top deck, while the fishermen sent the steamer off with bitter smiles.

"The price of fish has recently plummeted, so even the K.P.M. company has reduced shipping costs," Mr. Lin, who was traveling with me, told me as the boat departed.

I understood the scene of the captain's and the fishermen's expressions. In K City, my fisherman friends would have told me. If circumstances and a longer article allow, I will record these events!

After the boat set sail, the Dutch captain on the top deck picked up his hunting rifle and shot at fish in the river for fun. Hearing the sound of a gunshot, I glimpsed a fish in the river, wounded by the shot, raising its tail, its body flipping towards the center of the river, splashing the river water into a burst of waves, before sinking into the river and disappearing.

One shot after another rang out, and the river water continued with one burst of waves after another: and one fish after another, after sticking their heads out of the water to breathe, quietly sank into the water and disappeared without a trace. The fun and interest of this scene drew the attention of all the passengers on board, and the white people on the top deck erupted in bursts of laughter. But when I thought of the current plight of the Chinese fishermen, I felt a surge of disgust for the captain's entertainment after his frown, for some reason.

Mountain Pastoral (6) 207

— Ai Wu

The man threw the cigarette he was about to put in his mouth into the mountain ditch blocked by trees by the roadside. He stood up, grabbed the wooden stick under his feet, and pointed to the hillside not far away, smiling and said:

"Look, that's the business I do!"

The three people who were frightened by his raising the stick quickly looked towards the hillside. Among the short green trees, there was a tide like white waves—that was just some moving sheep.

Old Chen finally breathed a sigh of relief, but he was still speaking quickly, probably because he was suddenly happy.

"Well, this, this is a good occupation!"

Boss Qin sighed comfortably, greatly relieved, and immediately slapped his feverish face, blaming himself for saying such pitiful and embarrassing words just now.

Old Xu was so happy that he scratched his head and praised repeatedly:

"The sheep are really fat, really fat!"

The shepherd walked up the hillside path, singing:

"The wind is too strong,

The rain is too heavy,

I'm not afraid of shepherding on the hills!"

Someone on the hillside followed up with:

"I'm not afraid of heaven,

I'm not afraid of earth,

What does the emperor count for!"

The shepherd grabbed and sang again:

"What does the emperor count for?

Sheep's feet are dry,

Pig's tail!" (The End)

Dancing Marathon (6) 209

— (By L.T. Farrell of the United States) Translated by Yi Xian

One contestant after another gave up, the scope of the competition narrowed, but a month passed, and the days dragged on. One day, someone's birthday was celebrated on the dance floor. Another day, two newly acquainted contestants got engaged right there on the floor. This led to various crude jokes, one after another, some even talking about their wedding night. Later, this engaged couple was impulsed by lust and could not restrain themselves for a moment: the girls couldn't help but scream, and the girl was dragged off the floor. They both lost their qualifications and withdrew from the "Marathon." New fresh anecdotes came out again. One day, a girl pulled out a bunch of decayed teeth right there on the floor, and soon after, she was dizzy and spinning and dancing again. One day, because of the unemployment of both husband and wife, an Italian teenager who was dancing with his wife trampled his leg and developed a high fever. Although his eyes were red and swollen from the heat, and painful wrinkles were printed on his haggard face, he still limped and danced. After twelve hours, because the illness worsened, the notary forced him to withdraw from the competition.

Again and again, Tax reached out and received some unexpected income, and he could have been satisfied and wanted to leave the field, but he always persevered stubbornly. Like the other contestants, he often fell asleep in a daze, so he had to be awakened by external methods to keep him dancing. The male nurse patted his face with a warm towel, put his shoes on the wrong feet, rubbed him with an electric vibrator, dug his throat with his fingers, and trimmed the corns on his feet. At one point, his cough became severe, turning into chest pain. At one point, he was in a state of delirium for a full three weeks. His dance partner Mary also endured the same misery. They were still dancing. Day after day, night after night passed, and the contestants on the floor were reduced to thirteen pairs, ten pairs, eight pairs, five pairs, and finally only two pairs were left. Then Mary fainted, she was sent to the hospital, and Tax lost his qualification. They each received the second-place prize, two hundred and fifty yuan.

The methods of sleeping and making money were produced day by day, and he tried his best to make use of them, so all the contestants had more money. Everyone practiced their knife tricks, magic tricks or skills, a song, a dance, some kind of special skill, until they attracted everyone's attention, and the crowd threw money at them. One contestant was a rude country boy, originally from Lithuania, with a nasal accent. He shouted that shaving samples was his special skill. Tax, for his part, learned a kind of dance. Stores, theaters and cable companies also offered them fees, asking them to wear some kind of mark, or to wear undershirts with advertisements printed on both the front and back. They received money, and also received letters from admirers, often written in poor language, not much different from how Tax usually wrote. Various kinds of long-lasting viewers each selected the dancers on the floor and shouted encouragement to them.

Shen Bao Medical Weekly

The Problem of Lecithin for Smoking Cessation (The Problem of Lipoid for Smoking Cessation) (3) 210

— Pang Jingzhou

Explaining to the public, introducing to medical colleagues

However, the Health Department's sale of lecithin this time has the following mistakes and resulting malpractices:

(A) It did not first introduce the drug sample and Mr. Ma's literature to the medical community in advance, so that doctors had some doubts and indifference about this new brand of lecithin, and did not make a definite judgment. Some doctors, because they did not know what it was, casually abandoned it.

(B) Since the products of the Health Department use fashionable brands, and the tone in the instructions is very commercial, not in a tone for doctors, but only in a tone for smokers, so some people suspect that the Health Department's sale of this drug is a money-making career, with the intention of monopolizing the national smoking cessation drug, which has led to the imitation and abuse by speculative pharmacists, which was something the inventor, Mr. Ma, did not anticipate.

(C) Item 4 of the instructions did advise those taking lecithin to "preferably be guided by a doctor, or it is advisable to be hospitalized," but the psychology of smokers is not to be hospitalized and not to be guided by a doctor, so they buy lecithin to eat. So the lecithin sold is only for blind eating, only for trying, and the results are not good.

(D) Item 3 of the instructions, "After quitting smokers take this medicine, they will naturally and automatically reduce the amount of smoking every day, and feel disgusted," is the most sensational and fits the taste of our people for simple prescriptions. You must know that in the ideal of general smokers, it is not that they do not want to quit smoking, but they are afraid of how much pain it will cause. Every day they hope for a simple prescription like a spiritual response to save their chronic illness. Now they see lecithin, thinking it is a panacea, but this kind of smoker lacking self-control can take it at home, and reduce their smoking amount by themselves, (the life and thinking of people at home and smoking criminals in hospitals are completely different, no need to elaborate), so from hoping too much to disappointment, from disappointment to indiscriminate criticism, saying that lecithin is worthless, this kind of public opinion is all over society, and then asking doctors to prove the theory, it is too late, Chinese things are often like this.

(E) The Health Department thought that the level of smokers was very high, and attached a record form when selling it, asking the takers to fill it out themselves, but as a result, very few people filled it out, even if they filled it out, it was not complete, and even if it was complete, it was not sent to the Health Department, so that they still could not get the majority of statistics, and even disliked the poor taste of the Health Department's products, which was cited as incomplete research and criticized. So speculative pharmacists said that delicious lecithin was about to be launched on the market. What kind of pharmacology are we talking about in this situation?

(F) The Health Department did not prepare adequately before selling this drug, and did not adopt a registration method, so that the products could not meet the demand, and most of them were consumed by people who tried it and ate it blindly, while the users who were truly determined were turned away. Item 6 in the instructions strongly urged users to "not interrupt taking this drug," but as a result, the Health Department seemed to have broken faith with users because of the lack of goods, and people who did not understand blamed the drug itself, which was a bit of a misunderstanding.

(6) Is lecithin the best product for quitting smoking?

This question is probably what you are eager to know. However, to answer this question, it is necessary to be able to determine the efficacy of lecithin before comparing it with other drugs. Although the author has used a lot of lecithin, he has not been able to exhaust other methods. Even if you check the records of various countries, you may not be able to draw a conclusion. Because in this answer, there is still a major premise to determine the meaning of the two words "quit smoking." ——The so-called broad meaning of smoke poison includes morphine bills, red pills, white noodles, soil leather, faucet water, and all addictive substances similar to opium. In a narrow sense, it can be said that it only refers to the gun smoking of yattachee, yuntoo, Persian soil, and Rehe soil. In the past, Chinese people mostly used gun smoking. Now that the national economy is collapsing day by day. As a result, there are more and more quick-acting drug relief methods. However, compared with foreign countries. Gun smoking is still more common with us. They have very little. Foreign drug bans are strict. Anyone who is addicted is a criminal. If found, they will be forced to quit. Addicts are all criminals. And criminals are mostly hospitalized patients. Hospitalized patients are mostly those who swallow and inject morphine. Naturally, the smoking cessation methods they research are biased towards hospitalization. Moreover, for the sake of time and economy. It is more biased towards quick quitting. But my country is different. In the past, when the ban on smoking was relaxed. The literati used it to treat diseases. Beautifully named it Fushou Ointment. Prepared during social gatherings to respect guests. Treating it like Shaoxing wine. There are even idlers. I entrusted my life to this. Even treating it as an antique to appreciate. "The bucket is ripe, the gun is spiritual, the lamp comes out of the cover. The smoke is fragrant, the tea is ripe, the pillow is high." Fourteen characters. It is enough to describe the fun of weeping and groaning in the smoky clouds. Therefore, this group of gun smokers. Spiritual preferences. Than physical habits. The changes that can be traced in cells. Still deeper (according to the effect of opium. On the spirit to produce Euphoril. Translated as a kind of light feeling. This is perhaps not related to Mr. Ma's Golgi apparatus.) Therefore, in addition to considering adopting many established methods in the world. It seems necessary to consider the needs of gun smokers, Mr. Ma Wen Zhao tried lecithin this time. I feel this thing. Or closer to the truth than other methods. He really had great aspirations. But he did not consider himself above all methods, especially the results he obtained in the hospital. For a few of the most comfortable smokers. Does not bear any mission. The author of this article is now in the industry. So I am closer to this kind of smoker. What I have seen and heard. Or different from Mr. Ma. Therefore, I summarize the experience of using lecithin as follows. (1) Lecithin does not have any major malpractices. Only those who cannot tolerate its taste have minor vomiting. Among the several people who had diarrhea after taking it. Half of them had dysentery. The diarrhea stopped after stopping the medicine. (2) All those who took lecithin gained weight. The amount of increase varies. (3) There is one person who abandoned the smoking gun and only replaced it with lecithin. There are no symptoms of addiction such as tears and nasal discharge. But the spirit is decadent. (4) When smokers automatically reduce smoking when taking lecithin. The first one or two weeks decreased very quickly. It becomes difficult after entering. Therefore, many people stopped halfway. It should be handled by a doctor immediately. (5) Those who take lecithin for a long time and then take opium substitutes. The tolerance is generally not reduced. (6) All those who have taken lecithin and have reduced to smoking two or three puffs a day. If there is no automatic determination (firm will.) And other dynamic determination (those who have a reason to be forced to quit). Still cannot quit addiction. In ordinary families. Only persuade smokers not to quit hard. Almost no one can represent the doctor to limit the amount of smoking for them. (7) According to Mr. Ma, although he gave patients gun smoking in the hospital. However, this kind of gun smoking is already under supervision. Not the most satisfactory thing for addicts. Then Mr. Ma's principle. It is "no need for opium after taking lecithin." Not "cannot be exposed to opium again after taking lecithin." So the word "and produce disgust" in the Health Department's instructions. A little too much. And many smokers. I feel that when it is reduced to two or three tubes. Not only do they not feel disgusted. And love is more constant. So they do not trust lecithin. (8) If you use substitutes to quit smoking. And take lecithin at the same time. Then the effect is easy and fast, this is Mr. Ma's initial test method.

Since the scope of poisonous substances is very wide. Moreover, the methods are not limited to gun smoking. The environment of the breathers is also different. So the method of correction. Do not be rigid. Scholars in the past have studied Gongxiang. The author once saw the book "The Opium Problem 1928 (The Committee on Drug Addictions in Collaboration with the Bureau of Social Hygiene)" published jointly by the American "Drug Addiction Research Committee and the Public Health Bureau" in 1928. It is rich in literature from various countries. The effects of opium on the spirit, cells and body are explored to the fullest. Mr. Ma's theory of the Golgi apparatus is only one end of this book. This book is accompanied by the treatment methods of various countries.

The Importance of Vitamins to Life (II) 211

— Zhong Zhihe

Effects on the Human Body: (1) Protects the human body from scurvy; (2) Essential for bone metabolism; (3) Essential for the formation and maintenance of teeth.

Consequences of Deficiency or Absence:

(1) Suffering from scurvy, leading to the following phenomena:

(a) Easy bleeding in mucous membranes, skin, joints, limbs, and bone marrow.

(b) Gum deterioration, such as becoming spongy and frequently bleeding or ulcerating.

(c) Muscle and tissue bleeding.

(d) Joint and limb pain and swelling.

(e) Bones becoming brittle, leading to spontaneous fractures.

(2) Removal of lime from bones (Decalcification of bones).

(3) Delayed tooth eruption.

(4) Loose teeth, prone to falling out.

(5) Weight loss.

(6) Fatigue.

(7) Loss of appetite.

(8) Depressed and pale complexion.

Vitamin D (Vitamin D)

Also known as anti-rickets vitamin (Anti-Rachitic)

Effects on the Human Body:

(1) Regulates the absorption and metabolism of bone components, such as calcium and phosphorus.

(2) Regulates the metabolism of metallic salts in teeth and bones.

(3) Taking it during pregnancy can prevent rickets in infants, making it an indispensable product.

(4) Promotes bone fracture healing and strengthens teeth.

(5) Increases resistance to bacterial and parasitic diseases, thus improving conditions like progressive muscular atrophy, senile dementia, and certain gynecological disorders.

Consequences of Deficiency or Absence:

(1) Suffering from rickets or osteomalacia.

(2) Bone deformities (Deformity of bones).

(a) Bone brittleness and softening, often due to calcium deficiency in adults, leading to osteomalacia (commonly seen in India, China, and the Balkan Peninsula).

(b) Swollen wrists and elbows or arthritis.

(c) Rib joints developing bead-like enlargements.

(d) Bulging forehead.

(e) Softening of the skull bones.

(f) Delayed closure of fontanelles.

(g) Chest and pelvic bone deformities.

(h) Prone to bowlegs (Bowlegs).

(3) Generalized muscle, cartilage, and bone weakness, as well as nervous system instability.

(4) Due to lack of absorption, bone components like calcium and phosphorus are retained and deposited in the body.

(5) Reduces the levels of calcium and phosphorus in bones and blood.

(6) Tooth decay and increased susceptibility to cavities, as well as a tendency to develop alveolar pyorrhea.

Effects on the Human Body:

(1) Crucial for normal reproductive function.

(a) Essential for the maturation of normal male reproductive cells.

Consequences of Deficiency or Absence:

Leading to reproductive deficiency and infertility.

(a) In males, degeneration of the germinal epithelium of the reproductive system.

(b) In females, insufficient placental function.

(c) Affected pregnancy (leading to infant death or absorption and dissipation).

There are dozens of kinds. And Japan's Antimorchin and the recently popular plasma therapy are not included. (Note: Correcting the nervous system's addiction cannot be separated from the issue of time. Therefore, hypnosis is used to allow the smoker's period of suffering to pass in a state of sleep. Moreover, tonics are also frequently used. Thus, prescriptions using Strychnine are commonly seen. Even the commonly used Ci Bao Ming and other medications on the market are merely aids to the spirit and do not contain any narcotics. This is included here because many people misunderstand.) If we limit the amount of smoking for those who want to quit, then are the old Lin Zexu methods of China and methods like salt-fried rice flour with raw tobacco not effective? As for psychotherapy, how can we know that the immortal water from the Jigong altar is not helping a small number of people quit? However, practicing physicians on the market, in order to cater to the comfortable smokers, always cannot escape the trap of substitutes. Since three years ago, the plasma injection method (i.e., the currently called autologous blood serum injection method) used in France to quit drinking was promoted to Shanghai, and a certain general also used this method to quit smoking and went abroad. Therefore, it became a fad for a time. When egg yolk lecithin came on the market, it seemed like there was a three-legged race. Smoking cessation hospitals on the sea often claimed in their advertisements, "This hospital is superior in all three methods," etc. It really looks down on the scientific world too much. Each has its own reasons and value. Patients have different levels of addiction, and the speed of effectiveness varies. This article is limited to a brief explanation and cannot describe them one by one. Let me give a few documents related to Mr. Ma's method below. (1) In 1922, the German F.A. Looks mentioned the chemical relationship between morphine and egg yolk lecithin. (2) In 1925, the German Ph. Klee and O. Grossman used Cholin, which is a substance containing egg yolk lecithin. (2) In 1926, Alexander Lambert and Frederick Tilney used a kind of prepared medicine called Narcosan to quit smoking. One-third of the things contained inside are the lipoid substances in soybeans and cottonseed. It's simply like the products of the current Department of Health. (4) Last year, the French magazine Bulletine de medicine 1934 B XT. published an article entitled Procedede Deintoxication rapide des morphinomanes par les lmulsiones de lipoides, which described the use of lipoid emulsions and other oils injected into the muscles, requiring five injections a day, five centimeters each time, to quickly quit morphine addiction in five to seven days. His theory is to use lipoid substances to remove the old addiction of the nervous system, which is quite similar to Loofs' theory. But this method of use is only suitable for hospitalized patients.
